Enter the GHOAST OF ANDREA and with him REUENGE, False, Not marching now in fields of Thrasymene,Of man’s first disobedience and the fruit
GHOAST  When this eternall substance of my soule, False,,
Did liue imprisond in my wanton flesh, False,,
Ech in their function seruing others need, False,,
I was a courtier in the Spanish court, False,,
My name was Don Andrea my discent, False,,
Though not ignoble yet inferiour far, False,,
To gratious fortunes of my tender youth, False,,
For there in prime and pride of all my yeeres, False,,
By duteous seruice and deseruing loue, False,,
In secret I possest a worthy dame, False,,
Which hight sweet Belimperia by name, False,,
But in the haruest of my sommer ioyes, False,,
Deaths winter nipt the blossomes of my blisse, False,,
Forcing diuorce betwixt my loue and me, False,,
For in the late conflict with Portingale, False,,
My valour drew me into dangers mouth, False,,
Till life to death made passage through my wounds, False,,
When I was slaine my soule descended straight, False,,
To passe the flowing streame of Archeron, False,,
But churlish Charon only boatman there, False,,
Said that my rites of buriall not performde, False,,
I might not sit amongst his passengers, False,,
Ere Sol had slept three nights in Thetis lap, False,,
And slakte his smoaking charriot in her floud, False,,
By Don Horatio our knightmarshals sonne, False,,
My funerals and obsequies were done, False,,
Then was the fariman of hell content, False,,
To passe me ouer to the slimie strond, False,,
That leades to fell Auernus ougly waues, False,,
There pleasing Cerberus with honied speech, False,,
I past the perils of the formost porch, False,,
Not farre from hence amidst ten thousand soules, False,,
Sate Minos Eacus and Rhadamant, False,,
To whome no sooner gan I make approach, False,,
To craue a pasport for my wandring ghost, False,,
But Minos in grauen leaues of lotterie, False,,
Drew forth the manner of my life and death, False,,
This knight quoth he both liud and died in loue, False,,
And for his loue tried fortune of the warres, False,,
And by warres fortune lost both loue and life, False,,
Why then said Eacus convey him hence, False,,
To walke with lovers in our field of loue, False,,
And the course of euerlasting time, False,,
Vnder greene mirtletrees and cipresse shades, False,,
No no said Rhadamant it were not well, False,,
With louing soules to place a martialist, False,,
He died in warre and must to martiall fields, False,,
Where wounded Hector liues in lasting paine, False,,
And Achilles Mermedons do scoure the plaine, False,,
Then Minos mildest censor of the three, False,,
Made this deuice to end the difference, False,,
Send him quoth he to our infernall king, False,,
To dome him as best seemes his Maiestie, False,,
To this effect my pasport straight was drawne, False,,
In keeping on my way to Plutos court, False,,
Through dreadfull shades of euerglooming night, False,,
I saw more sights than thousand tongues can tell, False,,
Or pennes can write or mortall harts can think, False,,
Three waies there were that on the right hand side, False,,
Was ready way vnto the foresaid fields, False,,
Where louers liue and bloudie martialists, False,,
But either sort containd within his bounds, False,,
The left hand path declining fearfuly, False,,
Was ready downfall to the deepest hell, False,,
Where bloudie Furies shakes their whips of steele, False,,
And poore Ixion turnes an endles wheele, False,,
Where vsurers are choakt with melting golde, False,,
And wantons are imbraste with ougly snakes, False,,
And murderers groane with neuerkilling wounds, False,,
And periured wights scalded in boiling lead, False,,
And all foule sinnes with torments ouerwhelmd, False,,
Twixt these two waies I trod the middle path, False,,
Which brought me to the faire Elizian greene, False,,
In midst whereof there standes a stately towre, False,,
The walles of brasse the gates of adamant, False,,
Heere finding Pluto with his Proserpine, False,,
I shewed my pasport humbled on my knee, False,,
Whereat faire Proserpine began to smile, False,,
And begd that onely she might giue me doome, False,,
Pluto was pleasd and sealde it with a kisse, False,,
Forthwith Reuenge she rounded thee in th eare, False,,
And bad thee lead me though the gates of horn, False,,
Where dreames haue passage in the silent night, False,,
No sooner had she spoke but we weere heere, False,,
I wot not how in the twinkling of an eye, False,,
REUENGE  Then know Andrea that thou ariud, False,,
Where thou shalt see the author of thy death, False,,
Don Balthazar the prince of Portingale, False,,
Depriud of life by Belimperia, False,,
Heere sit we downe to see the misterie, False,,
And serue for Chorus in this tragedie, False,,
Enter SPANISH KING GENERALL CASTILLE HIERONIMO, False,,
KING  Now say lord generall how fares our campe, False,,
GEN  All wel my soueraigne liege except some few, False,,
That are deceast by fortune of the warre, False,,
KING  But what portends thy cheerefull countenance, False,,
And posting to our presence this in hast, False,,
Speak man  hath fortune giuen vs victorie, False,,
GEN  Victorie my liege and that with little losse, False,,
KING  Out Portugals will pay vs tribute then, False,,
GEN  Tribute and wonted homage therewithall, False,,
KING  Then blest be Heauen and Guider of the heauens, False,,
From whose faire influence such iustice flowes, False,,
CAST  O multum dilecte Deo tibi militat aether, False,,
Et coniuratae curato poplite gentes, False,,
Succumbent recto soror est victoria iuris, False,,
KING  Thanks to my loving brother of Castille, False,,
But generall vnfolde in breefe discourse, False,,
Your forme of battell and your warres successe, False,,
That adding all the pleasure of thy newes, False,,
Vnto the height of former happines, False,,
With deeper wage and gentile dignitie, False,,
We may reward thy blisfull chiualrie, False,,
GEN  Where Spaine and Portingale do ioyntly knit, False,,
Their frontiers leaning on each others bound, False,,
There met our armies in the proud aray, False,,
Both furnisht well both full of hope and feare, False,,
Both menacing alike with daring showes, False,,
Both vaunting sundry colours of deuice, False,,
Both cheerly sounding trumpets drums and fifes, False,,
Both raising dreadfull clamors to the skie, False,,
That valleis hils and riuers made rebound, False,,
And heauen itselfe was frighted with the sound, False,,
Our battels both were pitcht in squadron forme, False,,
Each corner strongly fenst with wings of shot, False,,
But ere we ioyned and came to push of pike, False,,
I brought a squadron of our readiest shot, False,,
From out our rearward to begin the fight, False,,
They brought another wing to incounter vs, False,,
Meanewhile our ordinance plaid on either side, False,,
And captaines stroue to haue their valours tride, False,,
Don Pedro their chiefe horsemens corlonell, False,,
Did with his cornet brauely make attempt, False,,
To break our order of our battell rankes, False,,
But Don Rogero worthy man of warre, False,,
Marcht forth against him with our musketiers, False,,
And stopt the mallice of his fell approach, False,,
While they maintaine hot skirmish too and fro, False,,
Both battailes ioyne and fall to handie blowes, False,,
Their violent shot resembling th oceans rage, False,,
When roaring lowd and with a swelling tide, False,,
It beats vpon the rampiers of huge rocks, False,,
And gapes to swallow neighborbounding lands, False,,
Now while Bellona rageth heere and there, False,,
Thick stormes of bullets ran like winters haile, False,,
And shiuered launces darke the troubled aire, False,,
Pede pes  cuspide cuspis, False,,
Arma sonant armis vir petiturque viro, False,,
On euery side drop captaines to the ground, False,,
And souldiers some illmaimde some slaine outright, False,,
Heere falls a body sundred from his head, False,,
There legs and armes lye bleeding on the grasse, False,,
Mingled with weapons and vnboweled steeds, False,,
That scattering ouerspread the purple plaine, False,,
In all this turmoyle three long hovres and more, False,,
The victory to neither part inclinde, False,,
Till Don Andrea with his braue lanciers, False,,
In their maine battell made so great a breach, False,,
That halfe dismaid the multitude retirde, False,,
But Balthazar the Portingales young prince, False,,
Brought rescue and encouragde them to stay, False,,
Heerehence the fight was eagerly renewd, False,,
And in that conflict was Andrea slaine—, False,,
Braue manatarms but weake to Balthazar, False,,
Yet while the prince insulting ouer him, False,,
Breathd out proud vaunts sounding to our reproch, False,,
Friendship and hardie valour ioyned in one, False,,
Prickt forth Horatio our knightmarshals sonne, False,,
To challenge forth that prince in single fight, False,,
Not long betweene these twain the fight indurde, False,,
But straight the prince was beaten from his horse, False,,
And forcst to yeeld him prisoner to his foe, False,,
When he was taken all the rest fled, False,,
And our carbines pursued them to death, False,,
Till Phoebus waning to the western deepe, False,,
Our trumpeters were chargd to sound retreat, False,,
KING  Thanks good lord general for these good newes, False,,
And for some argument of more to come, False,,
Take this and weare it for thy soueraignes sake, False,,
But tell me now  hast thou confirmed a peace, False,,
GEN  No peace my liege but peace conditionall, False,,
That if with homage tribute be well paid, False,,
The fury of your forces wilbe staide, False,,
And to this peace their viceroy hath subscribde, False,,
Giue the KING a paper, False,,
And made a solemne vow that during life, False,,
His tribute shalbe truely paid to Spaine, False,,
KING  These words these deeds become thy person wel, False,,
But now knightmarhsall frolike with thy king, False,,
For tis thy sonne that winnes this battels prize, False,,
HIERO  Long may he liue to serue my soueraigne liege, False,,
And soone decay unless he serue my liege, False,,
A trumpet afarre off, False,,
KING  Nor thou nor he shall dye without reward, False,,
What meanes this warning of this trumpets sound, False,,
GEN  This tels me that your Graces men of warre, False,,
Such as warres fortune hath reserud from death, False,,
Come marching on towards your royall seate, False,,
To show themselues before your Maiestie, False,,
For so gaue I in charge at my depart, False,,
Whereby by demonstration shall appeare, False,,
That all except three hundred or few more, False,,
Are safe returnd and by their foes inricht, False,,
The armie enters BALTHAZAR betweene LORENZO, False,,
and HORATIO captiue, False,,
KING  A gladsome sight  I long to see them heere, False,,
They enter and passe by, False,,
Was that the warlike prince of Portingale, False,,
That by our nephew was in triumph led, False,,
GEN  It was my liege the prince of Portingale, False,,
KING  But what was he that on the other side, False,,
Held him by th arme as partner of the prize, False,,
HIERO  That was my sonne my gracious soueraigne, False,,
Of whome though from his tender infancie, False,,
My louing thoughts did neuer hope but well, False,,
He neuer pleasd his fathers eyes till now, False,,
Nor fild my hart with ouercloying ioyes, False,,
KING  Goe let them march once more about these walles, False,,
That staying them we may conferre and talke, False,,
With our braue prisoner and his double guard, False,,
Hieoronimo it greatly pleaseth vs, False,,
That in our victorie thou haue a share, False,,
By vertue of thy worthy sonnes exploit, False,,
Bring hether the young prince of Portingale, False,,
The rest martch on but ere they be dismist, False,,
We will bestow on euery soldier, False,,
Two duckets and on euery leader ten, False,,
That they may know our largesse welcomes them, False,,
Exeunt all the army but BALTHAZAR, False,,
LORENZO and HORATIO, False,,
KING  Welcome Don Balthazar  Welcome nephew, False,,
And thou Horatio thou art welcome too, False,,
Young prince although thy fathers hard misdeedes, False,,
In keeping backe the tribute that he owes, False,,
Deserue but euill measure at our hands, False,,
Yet shalt thou know that Spaine is honorable, False,,
BALT  The trespasse that my father made in peace, False,,
Is now controlde by fortune of the warres, False,,
And cards once dealt it bootes not aske why so, False,,
His men are slaine—a weakening to his realme, False,,
His colours ceazd—a blot vnto his name, False,,
His sonne distrest—a corsiue to his hart, False,,
These punishments may cleare his late offence, False,,
KING  I Balthazar if he obserue this truce, False,,
Our peace will grow the stronger for these warres, False,,
Meanewhile liue thou though not in libertie, False,,
Yet free from bearing any seruile yoake, False,,
For in our hearing thy deserts were great, False,,
And in our sight thyselfe art gratious, False,,
BALT  And I shall studie to deserue this grace, False,,
KING  But tell me—for their holding makes me doubt, False,,
To Which of these twaine art thou prisoner, False,,
LOR  To me my liege, False,,
HOR                   To me my soueraigne, False,,
LOR  This hand first tooke his courser by the raines, False,,
HOR  But first my launce did put him from his horse, False,,
LOR  I ceazd the weapon and enioyde it first, False,,
HOR  But first I forcd him lay his weapons downe, False,,
KING Let goe his arm vpon my priviledge, False,,
Say worthy prince  to whether didst thou yeeld, False,,
BALT  To him in curtesie to this perforce, False,,
He spake me faire this other gaue me strokes, False,,
He promisde life this other threatned death, False,,
He wan my loue this other conquerd me, False,,
And truth to say I yeeld myselfe to both, False,,
HIERO  But that I know your Grace is iust and wise, False,,
And might seeme partiall in this difference, False,,
Inforct by nature and by law of armes, False,,
My tongue should plead for young Horatios right, False,,
He hunted well that was a lyons death, False,,
Not he that in a garment wore his skin, False,,
So hares may pull dead lyons by the beard, False,,
KING  Content thee marshall thou shalt haue no wrong, False,,
And for thy sake thy sonne shall want to right, False,,
Will both abide the censure of my doome, False,,
LOR  I craue no better than your Grace awards, False,,
HOR  Nor I although I sit beside my right, False,,
KING  Then by iudgement thus your strife shall end, False,,
You both deserue and both shall haue reward, False,,
Nephew thou tookst his weapons and his horse, False,,
His weapons and his horse are thy reward, False,,
Horatio thou didst force him first to yeeld, False,,
His ransome therefore is thy valours fee, False,,
Appoint the sum as you shall both agree, False,,
But nephew thou shalt haue the prince in guard, False,,
For thine estate best fitteth such a guest, False,,
Horatios house were small for all his traine, False,,
Yet in regard they substance passeth his, False,,
And that iust guerdon may befall desert, False,,
To him we yeeld the armour of the prince, False,,
How likes don Balthazar of this deuice, False,,
BALT  Right well my liege if this prouizo were, False,,
That Don Horatio beare vs company, False,,
Whome I admire and loue for chiualrie, False,,
KING  Horatio leaue him not that loues thee so, False,,
Now let vs hence to see our souldiers paide, False,,
And feast our prisoner as our friendly guest, False,,
Portugal  the VICEROYS palace, False,,
Enter VICEROY ALEXANDRO VILLUPPO, False,,
VICE  Is our embassadour dispatcht for Spaine, False,,
ALEX  Two daies my liege are past since his depart, False,,
VICE  And tribute paiment gone along with him, False,,
ALEX  I my good lord, False,,
VICE  Then rest we heere awhile in our vnrest, False,,
And feede our sorrowes with inward sighes, False,,
For deepest cares break neuer into teares, False,,
But wherefore sit I in a regall throne, False,,
This better fits a wretches endles moane, False,,
Yet this is higher then my fortunes reach, False,,
And therefore better then my state deserues, False,,
Falles to the grounde, False,,
I I this earth image of melancholly, False,,
Seeks him whome fates adiudge to miserie, False,,
Heere let me lye  Now am I at the lowest, False,,
Qui iacet in terra non habet vnde cadat, False,,
In me concumpsit vires fortuna nocendo, False,,
Nil superest vt iam possit obesse magis, False,,
Yes Fortune may bereaue me of my crowne—, False,,
Heere take it now let Fortune doe her worst, False,,
She shall now rob me of this sable weed, False,,
O no she enuies none but pleasent things, False,,
Such is the folly of despightfull chance, False,,
Fortune is blinde and sees not my deserts, False,,
So is she deafe and heares not my laments, False,,
And coulde she heare yet is she willfull mad, False,,
And therefore will not pittie my distresse, False,,
Suppose that she coulde pittie me what then, False,,
What helpe can be expected at her hands, False,,
Whose foote is standing on a rowling stone, False,,
And minde more mutable then fickle windes, False,,
Why waile I then wheres hope of no redresse, False,,
O yes complaining makes my greefe seeme lesse, False,,
My late ambition hath distaind my faith, False,,
My breach of faith occaisioned bloudie warres, False,,
Those bloudie warres haue spent my treasurie, False,,
And with my treasurie my peoples blood, False,,
And with the blood my ioy and best beloued—, False,,
My best beloued my sweet and onely sonne, False,,
O wherefore went I not to warre myselfe, False,,
The cause was mine I might haue died for both, False,,
My yeeres were mellow but his young and greene, False,,
My death were naturall but his was forced, False,,
ALEX  No doubt my liege but still the prince suruiues, False,,
VICE  Suruiues  I where, False,,
ALEX  In Spaine a prisoner by michance of warre, False,,
VICE  Then they haue slaine him for his fathers fault, False,,
ALEX  That were a breach to common lawe of armes, False,,
VICE  They recke no lawes that meditate reuenge, False,,
ALEX  His ransomes worth will stay from foule reuenge, False,,
VICE  No if he liued the newes would soone be heere, False,,
VILLUP  My soueraign pardon the author of ill newes, False,,
And Ile bewray the fortune of thy sonne, False,,
VICE  Speake on Ile guerdon thee whatere it be, False,,
Mine eare is ready to receiue ill newes, False,,
My hart growne hard gainst mischiefes battery, False,,
Stand vp I say and tell thy tale at large, False,,
VILLUP  Then heare that truth which these mine eies have seene, False,,
When both the armies were in battell ioyned, False,,
Don Balthazar amidst the thickest troupes, False,,
To winne renowme did wondrous feats of armes, False,,
Amongst the rest I saw him handtohand, False,,
In single fight with their lord generall, False,,
Till Alexandro that heere counterfeits, False,,
Vnder the colour of a duteous freend, False,,
Discharged a pistol at the princes back, False,,
As though he would haue slaine their generall, False,,
But therwithall Don Balthazar fell downe, False,,
And when he fell then we began to flie, False,,
But had he liued the day had sure bene ours, False,,
ALEX  O wiched forgerie  O traiterous miscreant, False,,
VICE  Hold thou thy peace  But now Villuppo say, False,,
Where then became the carkasse of my sonne, False,,
VILLUP  I saw them drag it to the Spanish tents, False,,
VICE  I I my nightly dreames haue tolde me this, False,,
Thou false vnkinde vnthankfull traiterous beast, False,,
Wherein had Balthazar offended thee, False,,
That thou should betray him to our foes, False,,
Wast Spanish golde that bleared so thine eyes, False,,
That thou couldst see no part of our deserts, False,,
Perchance because thou art Terseraes lord, False,,
Thou hadst some hope to weare this diademe, False,,
If first my sonne and then myselfe were slaine, False,,
But thy ambitious thought shall breake thy neck, False,,
I this was it that made thee spill his bloud, False,,
Take the crowne and put it on againe, False,,
But Ile now weare it till they bloud be spilt, False,,
ALEX  Vouchsafe dread soueraigne to heare me speak, False,,
VICE  Away with him  his sight is second hell, False,,
Keepe him till we determine his death, False,,
If Balthazar be dead he shall not liue, False,,
Villuppo follow vs for thy reward, False,,
VILLUP  Thus haue I with an enuious forged tale, False,,
Deceiued the king betraid mine enemy, False,,
And hope for guerdon of my villany, False,,
Enter HORATIO and BELIMPERIA, False,,
BEL  Signior Horatio this is the place and houre, False,,
Wherein I must intreat thee to relate, False,,
The circumstance of Don Andreas death, False,,
Who liuing was my garlands sweetest flower, False,,
And in his death hath buried my delights, False,,
HOR  For loue of him and seruice to yourself, False,,
Ile not refuse this heauy dolefull charge, False,,
Yet teares and sighes I feare will hinder me, False,,
When both our armies were enioynd in fight, False,,
Your worthie chiualier admist the thikst, False,,
For glorious cause still aiming at the fairest, False,,
Was at the last by yong Don Balthazar, False,,
Encountered handtohand  Their fight was long, False,,
Their harts were great their clamours menacing, False,,
Their strength alike their strokes both dangerous, False,,
But wrathfull Nemesis that wicked power, False,,
Enuying at Andreas praise and worth, False,,
Cut short his life to end his praise and woorth, False,,
She she herselfe disguisde in armours maske, False,,
As Pallas was before proud Pergamus, False,,
Brought in a fresh supply of halberdiers, False,,
Which pauncht his horse and dingd him to the ground, False,,
Then yong Don Balthazar with ruthles rage, False,,
Taking aduantage of his foes distresse, False,,
Did finish what his halberdiers begun, False,,
And left not till Andreas life was done, False,,
Then though too late incenst with iust remorce, False,,
I with my band set foorth against the prince, False,,
And brought him prisoner from his halbardiers, False,,
BEL  Would thou hadst slaine him that so slew my loue, False,,
But then was Don Andreas carkasse lost, False,,
HOR  No that was it for which I cheefely stroue, False,,
Nor stept I back till I recouerd him, False,,
I tooke him vp and wound him in mine armes, False,,
And welding him vnto my priuate tent, False,,
There laid him downe and dewd him with my teares, False,,
And sighed and sorrowed as became a freend, False,,
But neither freendly sorrow sighes and teares, False,,
Could win pale Death from his vsurped right, False,,
Yet this I did and lesse I could not doe, False,,
I saw him honoured with due funerall, False,,
This scarfe I pluckt from off his liueles arme, False,,
And wear it in remembrance of my freend, False,,
BEL  I know the scarfe would he had kept it still, False,,
For had he liued he would haue kept it still, False,,
And worne it for his Belimperias sake, False,,
For twas my fauour at his last depart, False,,
But now weare thou it both for him and me, False,,
For after him thou hast deserued it best, False,,
But for thy kindnes in his life and death, False,,
Be sure while Belimperias life endures, False,,
She will be Don Horatios thankfull freend, False,,
HOR  And madame Don Horatio will not slacke, False,,
Humbly to serue faire Belimperia, False,,
But now if your good liking stand thereto, False,,
Ile craue your pardon to goe seeke the prince, False,,
For so the duke your father gaue me charge, False,,
BEL  I goe Horatio leaue me heere alone, False,,
For solitude best fits my cheereles mood—, False,,
Yet what auailes to waile Andreas death, False,,
From whence Horatio proues my second loue, False,,
Had he not loued Andrea as he did, False,,
He could not sit in Belimperias thoughts, False,,
But how can loue finde harbour in my brest, False,,
Till I reuenge the death of my beloued, False,,
Yes second loue shall further my reuenge, False,,
Ile loue Horatio my Andreas freend, False,,
The more to spight the prince that wrought his end, False,,
And where Don Balthazar that slew my loue, False,,
He shall in rigour of my iust disdaine, False,,
Reape long repentance for his murderous deed—, False,,
For what wast els but murderous cowardise, False,,
So many to oppresse one valiant knight, False,,
Without respect of honour in the fight, False,,
And heere he comes that murdred my delight, False,,
Enter LORENZO and BALTHAZAR, False,,
LOR  Sister what meanes this melanchollie walke, False,,
BEL  That for awhile I wish no company, False,,
LOR  But heere the prince is come to visite you, False,,
BEL  That argues that he liues in libertie, False,,
BAL  No madam but in pleasing seruitude, False,,
BEL  Your prison then belike is your conceit, False,,
BAL  I by conceite my freedome is enthralde, False,,
BEL  Then with conceite enlarge yourselfe againe, False,,
BAL  What if conceite haue laid my hart to gage, False,,
BEL  Pay that you borrowed and recouer it, False,,
BAL  I die if it returne from whence it lyes, False,,
BEL  A hartles man and liue  A miracle, False,,
BAL  I lady loue can work such miracles, False,,
LOR  Tush tush my lord  let goe these ambages, False,,
And in plaine tearmes acquaint her with your loue, False,,
BEL  What bootes complaint when thers no remedy, False,,
BAL  Yes to your gracios selfe must I complaine, False,,
In whose faire answere lyes my remedy, False,,
On whose perfection all my thoughts attend, False,,
On whose aspect mine eyes finde beauties bowre, False,,
In whose translucent brest my hart is lodgde, False,,
BEL Alas my lord there but words of course, False,,
And but deuise to driue me from this place, False,,
She going in lets fall her gloue which, False,,
HORATIO comming out takes vp, False,,
HOR  Madame your gloue, False,,
BEL  Thanks good Horatio take it for thy paines, False,,
BAL  Signior Horatio stoopt in happie time, False,,
HOR  I reapt more grace that I deserud or hopd, False,,
LOR  My lord be not dismaid for what is past, False,,
You know that women oft are humerous, False,,
These clouds will ouerblow with little winde, False,,
Let me alone Ill scatter them myselfe, False,,
Meanewhile let vs deuise to spend the time, False,,
In some delightfull sports and reuelling, False,,

Enter VICEROY OF PORTINGALE NOBLES ALEXANDRO, False,,
VICEROY  Infortunate condition of kings, False,,
Seated amidst so many helples doubts, False,,
Firstwe are plast vpon extreamest height, False,,
And oft supplanted with exceeding hate, False,,
But euer subiect to the wheele of chance, False,,
And at our highest neuer ioy we so, False,,
As we doubt and dread our ouerthrow, False,,
So striueth not the waues with sundry winds, False,,
As fortune toyleth in the affaires of kings, False,,
That would be feard yet feare to be beloued, False,,
Sith feare and loue to kings is flatterie, False,,
For instance lordings look vpon your king, False,,
By hate depriued of his dearest sonne, False,,
The only hope of our successiue line, False,,
NOB  I had not thought that Alexandros hart, False,,
Had beene enuenomde with such extreame hate, False,,
But now I see that words haue seuerall workes, False,,
And theres no credit in the countenance, False,,
VIL  No for my lord had you beholde the traine, False,,
That fained loue had coloured in his lookes, False,,
When he in campe consorted Balthazar, False,,
Farre more inconstant had you thought the sunne, False,,
That howerly coasts the center of the earth, False,,
Then Alexandros purpose to the prince, False,,
VICE  No more Villuppo thou hast said enough, False,,
And with thy words thou saiest our wounded thoughts, False,,
Nor shall I longer dally with the world, False,,
Procrastinating Alexandros death, False,,
Goe some of you and fetch the traitor forth, False,,
That as he is condemned he may dye, False,,
Enter ALEXANDRO with a NOBLEMAN and, False,,
NOB In such extreames will nought but patience serue, False,,
ALEX  But in extreames what patience shall I vse, False,,
Nor discontents it me to leaue the world, False,,
With whome there nothing can preuaile but wrong, False,,
NOB  Yet hope the best, False,,
ALEX                         Tis heauen my hope, False,,
As for the earth it is too much infect, False,,
To yeeld me hope of any of her mould, False,,
VICE  Why linger ye bring froth that daring feend, False,,
And let him die for his accursed deed, False,,
ALEX  Not that I feare the extremitie of death—, False,,
For nobles cannot stoop to seruile feare—, False,,
Doo I O king thus discontented liue, False,,
But this O this torments my labouring soule, False,,
That thus I die suspected of a sinne, False,,
Whereof as Heauens haue knowne my secret thoughts, False,,
So am I free from this suggestion, False,,
VICE  No more I say to the tortures  when, False,,
Binde him and burne his body in those flames, False,,
They binde him to the stake, False,,
That shall prefigure those vnquenched fiers, False,,
Of Phlegiton prepared for his soule, False,,
ALEX  My guiltles death will be auengd on thee, False,,
On thee Villuppo that hath malisde thus, False,,
Or for thy meed hast falsely me accusde, False,,
VIL  Nay Alexandro if thou menace me, False,,
Ile lend a hand to send thee to the lake, False,,
Where those thy words shall perish with thy workes, False,,
Iniurious traitour monstrous homicide, False,,
EM  Stay  hold awhile  and heer with pardon of, False,,
His Maiestie lay hands vpon Villuppo, False,,
VICE  Embassadour what newes nath vrgd this sodain, False,,
EM  Know soueraigne lord that Balthazar doth liue, False,,
VICE  What saiest thou  liueth Balthazar our sonne, False,,
EM  Your Highnes sonne Lord Balthazar doth liue, False,,
And well intreated in the court of Spaine, False,,
Humbly commends him to your Maiestie, False,,
These eies beheld and these my followers, False,,
With these the letters of the kings commend, False,,
Are happie witnesses of his Highnes health, False,,
The KING lookes on the letters and proceeds, False,,
VICE reads  Thy sonne doth liue your tribute is receiud, False,,
Thy peace is made and we are satisfied, False,,
The rest resolue vpon as things proposde, False,,
For both our honors and they benefite, False,,

He giues him more letters, False,,

Against the life and reputation, False,,
Of noble Alexandro  come my lord vnbinde him, False,,
To ALEXANDRO  Let him vnbinde thee that is bounde to death, False,,
To make a quitall for thy discontent, False,,
ALEX  Dread lord in kindnes you could do no lesse, False,,
Vpon report of such a damned fact, False,,
But thus we see our innocence hath saud, False,,
The hopeles like which thou Villuppo sought, False,,
By thy suggestions to haue massacred, False,,

Falsely betray Lord Alexandros life, False,,
Him whom thou knowest that no vnkindenes els, False,,
But euen the slaughter of our deerest sonne, False,,
Could once haue moued vs to haue misconceaued, False,,
ALEX  Say trecherous Villuppo tell the King, False,,
Or wherein hath Alexandro vsed thee ill, False,,
VIL  Rent with remembrance of so foule a deed, False,,
My guiltie soule submits me to thy doome, False,,
For not for Alexandros iniuries, False,,
But for reward and hope to be preferd, False,,
Thus haue I shamelesly hazarded his life, False,,
VICE  Which villaine shalbe ransomed with thy death, False,,
And not so meane a torment as we heere, False,,
Deuised for him who thou saidst slew our sonne, False,,
But with the bitterest torments and extreames, False,,
That may be yet inuented for thine end, False,,
ALEXANDRO seemes to intreat, False,,
Intreat me not  Goe take the traitor hence, False,,
And Alexandro let vs honor thee, False,,
With publique notice of thy loyaltie, False,,
To end those things articulated heere, False,,
By our great lord the mightie king of Spaine, False,,
We with our councell will deliberate, False,,
Come Alexandro keepe vs company, False,,
Spain near the DUKEs castle, False,,
HIERO  Oh eies  no eies but fountains fraught with teares, False,,
Oh life no life but liuely fourme of death, False,,
Oh world no world but masse of publique wrongs, False,,
Confusde and filde with murder and misdeeds, False,,
Oh sacred heauens if this vnhallowed deed, False,,
If this inhumane and barberous attempt, False,,
If this incomparable murder thus, False,,
Of mine but now no more my sonne, False,,
Shall pass vnreueald and vnreuenged passe, False,,
How should we tearme your dealings to be iust, False,,
If you vniustly deale with those that in your iustice trust, False,,
The night sad secretary to my mones, False,,
With direfull visions wake my vexed soule, False,,
And with the wounds of my distresfull sonne, False,,
Solicite me for notice of his death, False,,
The ougly feends do sally forth of hell, False,,
And frame my hart with fierce inflamed thoughts, False,,
The cloudie day my discontents records, False,,
Early begins to regester my dreames, False,,
And driue me forth to seeke the murtherer, False,,
Eies life world heauens hel night and day, False,,
See search show send some man some meane that may, False,,
Whats heere a letter  Tush it is not so, False,,
A letter for Hieronimo, False,,
Reads  For want of incke receiue this bloudie writ, False,,
Me hath my haples brother hid from thee, False,,
Reuenge thyselfe on Balthazar and him, False,,
For these were they that murdered thy sonne, False,,
Hieronimo reuenge Horatios death, False,,
And better fare then Belimperia doth—, False,,
What meanes this vnexpected miracle, False,,
My sonne slaine by Lorenzo and the prince, False,,
What cause had they Horatio to maligne, False,,
Or what might mooue thee Belimperia, False,,
To accuse they brother had he beene the meane, False,,
Hieronimo beware  thou art betraide, False,,
And to intrap they life this traine is laide, False,,
Aduise thee therefore be not credulous, False,,
This is deuised to endanger thee, False,,
That thou by this Lorenzo shoulst accuse, False,,
And he for thy dishonour done show draw, False,,
Thy life in question and thy name in hate, False,,
Deare was the life of my beloved sonne, False,,
And of his death behoues me to be auengd, False,,
Then hazard not thine own Hieronimo, False,,
But liue teffect thy resolution, False,,
I therefore will by circumstances trie, False,,
What I can gather to confirme this writ, False,,
And harken neere the Duke of Castiles house, False,,
Close if I can with Belimperia, False,,
To listen more but nothing to bewray, False,,

This slie enquiry of Hieronimo, False,,
For Belimperia breeds suspition, False,,
And thus suspition boads a further ill, False,,

Nor shall they liue for me to feare their faith, False,,

Slaues are ordeined to no other end, False,,

PED  Now Pedringano bid thy pistoll holde, False,,

Enter BOY with the boxe, False,,
BOY  My maister hath forbidden me to look in this box and by, False,,
my troth tis likely if he had not warned me I should not haue had so, False,,
much idle time for wee menkinde in our minoritie are like women in, False,,
their vncertaintie that they are most forbidden they wil soonest, False,,
attempt so I now  By my bare honesty heeres nothing but the bare, False,,
emptie box  Were it not sin against secrecie I would say it were a, False,,

Or mine exclaimes that haue surcharged the aire, False,,
With ceasles plaints for my deceased sonne, False,,
The blustring winds conspiring with my words, False,,
At my lament haue moued to leaueless trees, False,,
Disroabde the medowes of their flowred greene, False,,
Made mountains marsh with springtides of my teares, False,,
And broken through the brazen gates of hell, False,,
Yet still tormented is my tortured soule, False,,
With broken sighes and restles passions, False,,
That winged mount and houering in the aire, False,,
Beat at the windowes of the brightest heauens, False,,
Soliciting for iustice and reuenge, False,,
But they are plact in those imperiall heights, False,,
Where countermurde with walles of diamond, False,,
I finde the place impregnable and they, False,,
Resist my woes and giue my words no way, False,,

The following is inserted in the   and  editions, False,,
HIER  Tis neither as you thinke nor as you thinke, False,,

These slippers are not mine they were my sonne Horatios, False,,
My sonne  And whats a sonne  A thing begot, False,,
Within a paire of minutes thereabout, False,,
A lump bred up in darknesse and doth serue, False,,
To ballance those light creatures we call women, False,,
And at nine monethes end creepes foorth to light, False,,
What is there yet in a sonne to make a father, False,,
Dote rave or runne mad  Being born it pouts, False,,
Cries and breeds teeth  What is there yet in a sonne, False,,
He must be fed be taught to goe and speake, False,,
I and yet  Why might not a man love, False,,
A calfe as well or melt in passion over, False,,
A frisking kid as for a sonne  Me thinkes, False,,
A young bacon or a fine smooth little horsecolt, False,,
Should moove a man as much as doth a son, False,,
For one of these in very little time, False,,
Will grow to some good use whereas a sonne, False,,
The more he growes in stature and in yeeres, False,,
The more unsquard unlevelled he appeares, False,,
Reckons his parents among the ranke of fooles, False,,
Strikes cares upon their heads with his mad ryots, False,,

This is a son  And what a losse were this, False,,

He lovd his loving parents he was my comfort, False,,

Enter HIERONIMO with a book in his hand, False,,
HIERO  Vindicta mihi, False,,
I heauen will be reuenged of euery ill, False,,
Nor will they suffer murder vnrepaide, False,,
Then stay Hieronimo attend their will, False,,
For mortall men may not appoint their time, False,,
Per scelus semper tutum est sceleribus iter, False,,
Strike and strike home where wrong is offred thee, False,,
For euils vnto ils conductors be, False,,
And deaths the worst of resultion, False,,
For he that thinks with patience to contend, False,,
To quiet life his life shall easily end, False,,
Fata si miseros iuuant habes selutem, False,,
Fata si vitam negant habes sepulchrum, False,,
If destinie thy miseries doe ease, False,,
Then hast thou health and happie shalt thou be, False,,
If destinie denie thee life Hieronimo, False,,
Yet shalt thou be assured of a tombe, False,,
If neither yet let this thy comfort be, False,,
Heauen couereth him that hath no buriall, False,,
And to conclude I will reuenge his death, False,,
But how  Not as the vulgare wits of men, False,,
With open but ineuitable ils, False,,
As by a secret yet a certaine meane, False,,
Which vnder kindeship wilbe cloked best, False,,
Wise men will take their opportunitie, False,,
Closely and safely fitting things to time, False,,
But in extreames aduantage hath no time, False,,
And therefore all times fit not for reuenge, False,,
Thus therefore will I rest me in unrest, False,,
Dissembling quiet in vnquietnes, False,,
Not seeming that I know their villanies, False,,
That my simplicitie may make them think, False,,
That ignorantly I will let all slip, False,,
For ignorance I wot and well they know, False,,
Remedium malorum iners est, False,,
Nor ought auailes it me to menace them, False,,
Who as a wintrie storme vpon a plaine, False,,
Will beare me downe with their nobilitie, False,,
No no Hieronimo thou must enioyne, False,,
Thine eies to obseruation and thy tung, False,,
To milder speeches then thy spirit affoords, False,,
Thy hart to patience and thy hands to rest, False,,

Hieronimo as when a raging sea, False,,

I will leaue not a root a stalke a tree, False,,

Accursed complot of my miserie, False,,
Fruitlesse foreuer may this garden be, False,,

The death of Aiax or some Romaine peer, False,,

, False,,To less than gods On the other side up rose

, False,,To waste eternal days in woe and pain
, False,,And reckonst thou thyself with spirits of Heaven
, False,,Helldoomed and breathst defiance here and scorn
, False,,Where I reign king and to enrage thee more
, False,,Thy king and lord Back to thy punishment
, False,,False fugitive and to thy speed add wings
, False,,Lest with a whip of scorpions I pursue
, False,,Thy lingering or with one stroke of this dart
, False,,Strange horror seize thee and pangs unfelt before
, False,,So spake the grisly terror and in shape
, False,,So speaking and so threatening grew tenfold
, False,,More dreadful and deform On the other side
, False,,Incensed with indignation Satan stood
, False,,Unterrified and like a comet burned
, False,,That fires the length of Ophiuchus huge
, False,,In the arctic sky and from his horrid hair
, False,,Shakes pestilence and war Each at the head
, False,,Leveled his deadly aim their fatal hands
, False,,No second stroke intend and such a frown
, False,,Each cast at the other as when two black clouds
, False,,With heavens artillery fraught came rattling on
, False,,Over the Caspian then stand front to front
, False,,Hovering a space till winds the signal blow
, False,,To join their dark encounter in midair
, False,,So frowned the mighty combatants that Hell
, False,,Grew darker at their frown so matched they stood
, False,,For never but once more was wither like
, False,,To meet so great a foe And now great deeds
, False,,Had been achieved whereof all Hell had rung
, False,,Had not the snaky Sorceress that sat
, False,,Fast by Hellgate and kept the fatal key
, False,,Risen and with hideous outcry rushed between
, False,,Oh father what intends thy hand she cried
, False,,Against thy only son What fury Oh son
, False,,Possesses thee to bend that mortal dart
, False,,Against thy fathers head And knowst for whom
, False,,For him who sits above and laughs the while
, False,,At thee ordained his drudge to execute
, False,,Whateer his wrath which he calls justice bids
, False,,His wrath which one day will destroy ye both
, False,,She spake and at her words the hellish pest
, False,,Forbore then these to her Satan returned
, False,,So strange thy outcry and thy words so strange
, False,,Thou interposest that my sudden hand
, False,,Prevented spares to tell thee yet by deeds
, False,,What it intends till first I know of thee
, False,,What thing thou art thus doubleformed and why
, False,,In this infernal vale first met thou callst
, False,,Me father and that phantasm callst my son
, False,,I know thee not nor ever saw till now
, False,,Sight more detestable than him and thee
, False,,T whom thus the portress of Hellgate replied
, False,,Hast thou forgot me then and do I seem
, False,,Now in thine eye so foul once deemed so fair
, False,,In Heaven when at the assembly and in sight

, False,,In bold conspiracy against Heavens King
, False,,All on a sudden miserable pain
, False,,Surprised thee dim thine eyes and dizzy swum
, False,,In darkness while thy head flames thick and fast
, False,,Threw forth till on the left side opening wide

, False,,Then shining heavenly fair a goddess armed
, False,,Out of thy head I sprung Amazement seized
, False,,All the host of Heaven back they recoiled afraid
, False,,At first and called me Sin and for a sign
, False,,Portentous held me but familiar grown
, False,,I pleased and with attractive graces won
, False,,The most averse thee chiefly who full oft
, False,,Thyself in me thy perfect image viewing
, False,,Becamst enamored and such joy thou tookst
, False,,With me in secret that my womb conceived
, False,,A growing burden Meanwhile war arose
, False,,And fields were fought in Heaven wherein remained
, False,,For what could else to our Almighty Foe
, False,,Clear victory to our part loss and rout
, False,,Through all the Empyrean Down they fell
, False,,Driven headlong from the pitch of Heaven down
, False,,Into this deep and in the general fall
, False,,I also at which time this powerful key
, False,,Into my hands was given with charge to keep
, False,,These gates for ever shut which none can pass
, False,,Without my opening Pensive here I sat
, False,,Alone but long I sat not till my womb
, False,,Pregnant by thee and now excessive grown
, False,,Prodigious motion felt and rueful throes
, False,,At last this odious offspring whom thou seest
, False,,Thine own begotten breaking violent way
, False,,Tore through my entrails that with fear and pain
, False,,Distorted all my nether shape thus grew
, False,,Transformed but he my inbred enemy
, False,,Forth issued brandishing his fatal dart
, False,,Made to destroy I fled and cried out Death
, False,,Hell trembled at the hideous name and sighed
, False,,From all her caves and back resounded Death
, False,,I fled but he pursued though more it seems
, False,,Inflamed with lust than rage and swifter far
, False,,Me overtook his mother all dismayed
, False,,And in embraces forcible and foul
, False,,Engendering with me of that rape begot
, False,,These yelling monsters that with ceaseless cry
, False,,Surround me as thou sawst hourly conceived
, False,,And hourly born with sorrow infinite
, False,,To me for when they list into the womb
, False,,That bred them they return and howl and gnaw
, False,,My bowels their repast then bursting forth
, False,,Afresh with conscious terrors vex me round
, False,,That rest or intermission none I find
, False,,Before mine eyes in opposition sits
, False,,Grim Death my son and foe who set them on
, False,,And me his parent would full soon devour
, False,,For want of other prey but that he knows
, False,,His end with mine involved and knows that I
, False,,Should prove a bitter morsel and his bane
, False,,Whenever that shall be so Fate pronounced
, False,,But thou Oh father I forewarn thee shun
, False,,His deadly arrow neither vainly hope
, False,,To be invulnerable in those bright arms
, False,,Through tempered heavenly for that mortal dint
, False,,Save he who reigns above none can resist
, False,,She finished and the subtle fiend his lore
, False,,Soon learned now milder and thus answered smooth
, False,,Dear daughter since thou claimst me for thy sire
, False,,And my fair son here showst me the dear pledge
, False,,Of dalliance had with thee in Heaven and joys
, False,,Then sweet now sad to mention through dire change
, False,,Befallen us unforeseen unthoughtof know
, False,,I come no enemy but to set free
, False,,From out this dark and dismal house of pain
, False,,Both him and thee and all the heavenly host
, False,,Of Spirits that in our just pretences armed
, False,,Fell with us from on high From them I go
, False,,This uncouth errand sole and one for all
, False,,Myself expose with lonely steps to tread
, False,,The unfounded Deep and through the void immense
, False,,To search with wandering quest a place foretold
, False,,Should be and by concurring signs ere now
, False,,Created vast and round a place of bliss
, False,,In the purlieus of Heaven and therein placed
, False,,A race of upstart creatures to supply
, False,,Perhaps our vacant room though more removed
, False,,Lest Heaven surcharged with potent multitude
, False,,Might hap to move new broils Be this or aught
, False,,Than this more secret now designed I haste
, False,,To know and this once known shall soon return
, False,,And bring ye to the place where thou and Death
, False,,Shall dwell at ease and up and down unseen
, False,,Wing silently the buxom air embalmed
, False,,With odors There ye shall be fed and filled
, False,,Immeasurably all things shall be your prey
, False,,He ceased for both seemed highly pleased and Death
, False,,Grinned horrible a ghastly smile to hear
, False,,His famine should be filled and blessed his maw
, False,,Destined to that good hour No less rejoiced
, False,,His mother bad and thus bespake her sire
, False,,The key of this infernal pit by due
, False,,And by command of Heavens allpowerful King
, False,,I keep by him forbidden to unlock
, False,,These adamantine gates against all force
, False,,Death ready stands to interpose his dart
, False,,Fearless to be oermatched by living might
, False,,But what owe I to his commands above
, False,,Who hates me and hath hither thrust me down
, False,,Into this gloom of Tartarus profound
, False,,To sit in hateful office here confined
, False,,Inhabitant of Heaven and heavenly born
, False,,Here in perpetual agony and pain
, False,,With terrors and with clamors compassed round
, False,,Of mine own brood that on my bowels feed

, False,,My being gavst me whom should I obey
, False,,But thee whom follow Thou wilt bring me soon
, False,,To that new world of light and bliss among

, False,,At thy right hand voluptuous as beseems
, False,,Thy daughter and thy darling without end
, False,,Thus saying from her side the fatal key
, False,,Sad instrument of all our woe she took
, False,,And towards the gate rolling her bestial train
, False,,Forthwith the huge portcullis high updrew
, False,,Which but herself not all the stygian powers
, False,,Could once have moved then in the keyhole turns
, False,,The intricate wards and every bolt and bar
, False,,Of massy iron or solid rock with ease
, False,,Unfastens On a sudden open fly
, False,,With impetuous recoil and jarring sound
, False,,The infernal doors and on their hinges grate
, False,,Harsh thunder that the lowest bottom shook
, False,,Of Erebus She opened but to shut
, False,,Excelled her power the gates wide open stood
, False,,That with extended wings a bannered host
, False,,Under spread ensigns marching might pass through
, False,,With horse and chariots ranked in loose array
, False,,So wide they stood and like a furnacemouth
, False,,Cast forth redounding smoke and ruddy flame
, False,,Before their eyes in sudden view appear
, False,,The secrets of the hoary deep a dark
, False,,Illimitable ocean without bound
, False,,Without dimension where length breadth and height
, False,,And time and place are lost where eldest night
, False,,And chaos ancestors of nature hold
, False,,Eternal anarchy amidst the noise
, False,,Of endless wars and by confusion stand
, False,,For hot cold moist and dry four champions fierce
, False,,Strive here for mastery and to battle bring
, False,,Their embryon atoms they around the flag
, False,,Of each his faction in their several clans
, False,,Lightarmed or heavy sharp smooth swift or slow
, False,,Swarm populous unnumbered as the sands
, False,,Of Barca or Cyrenes torrid soil
, False,,Levied to side with warring winds and poise
, False,,Their lighter wings To whom these most adhere
, False,,He rules a moment Chaos umpire sits
, False,,And by decision more embroils the fray
, False,,By which he reigns next him high arbiter
, False,,Chance governs all Into this wild abyss
, False,,The womb of nature and perhaps her grave
, False,,Of neither sea nor shore nor air nor fire
, False,,But all these in their pregnant causes mixed
, False,,Confusedly and which thus must ever fight
, False,,Unless the Almighty Maker them ordain
, False,,His dark materials to create more worlds
, False,,Into this wild Abyss the wary Fiend
, False,,Stood on the brink of Hell and looked a while
, False,,Pondering his voyage for no narrow frith
, False,,He had to cross Nor was his ear less pealed
, False,,With noises loud and ruinous to compare
, False,,Great things with small than when Bellona storms
, False,,With all her battering engines bent to rase
, False,,Some capital city or less than if this frame
, False,,Of Heaven were falling and these elements
, False,,In mutiny had from her axle torn
, False,,The steadfast Earth At last his sailbroad vans
, False,,He spread for flight and in the surging smoke
, False,,Uplifted spurns the ground thence many a league
, False,,As in a cloudy chair ascending rides
, False,,Audacious but that seat soon failing meets
, False,,A vast vacuity All unawares
, False,,Fluttering his pennons vain plumbdown he drops
, False,,Ten thousand fathom deep and to this hour
, False,,Down had been falling had not by ill chance
, False,,The strong rebuff of some tumultuous cloud
, False,,Instinct with fire and nitre hurried him
, False,,As many miles aloft That fury stayed
, False,,Quenched in a boggy Syrtis neither sea
, False,,Nor good dry land nigh foundered on he fares
, False,,Treading the crude consistence half on foot
, False,,Half flying behooves him now both oar and sail
, False,,As when a gryphon through the wilderness
, False,,With winged course oer hill or moory dale
, False,,Pursues the Arimaspian who by stealth
, False,,Had from his wakeful custody purloined
, False,,The guarded gold so eagerly the fiend
, False,,Oer bog or steep through strait rough dense or rare
, False,,With head hands wings or feet pursues his way
, False,,And swims or sinks or wades or creeps or flies
, False,,At length a universal hubbub wild
, False,,Of stunning sounds and voices all confused
, False,,Borne through the hollow dark assaults his ear
, False,,With loudest vehemence Thither he plies
, False,,Undaunted to meet there whatever power
, False,,Or spirit of the nethermost Abyss
, False,,Might in that noise reside of whom to ask
, False,,Which way the nearest coast of darkness lies
, False,,Bordering on light when straight behold the throne
, False,,Of Chaos and his dark pavilion spread
, False,,Wide on the wasteful deep With him enthroned
, False,,Sat sablevested Night eldest of things
, False,,The consort of his reign and by them stood
, False,,Orcus and Ades and the dreaded name
, False,,Of Demogorgon Rumour next and Chance
, False,,And Tumult and Confusion all embroiled
, False,,And Discord with a thousand various mouths
, False,,To whom Satan turning boldly thus Ye powers
, False,,And spirtis of this nethermost Abyss
, False,,Chaos and ancient Night I come no spy
, False,,With purpose to explore or to disturb
, False,,The secrets of your realm but by constraint
, False,,Wandering this darksome desert as my way
, False,,Lies through your spacious empire up to light
, False,,Alone and without guide half lost I seek
, False,,What readiest path leads where your gloomy bounds
, False,,Confine with Heaven or if some other place
, False,,From your dominion won the Ethereal King
, False,,Possesses lately thither to arrive
, False,,I travel this profound Direct my course
, False,,Directed no mean recompense it brings
, False,,To your behoove if I that region lost
, False,,All usurpation thence expelled reduce
, False,,To her original darkness and your sway
, False,,Which is my present journey and once more
, False,,Erect the standard there of ancient night
, False,,Yours be the advantage all mine the revenge
, False,,Thus Satan and him thus the anarch old
, False,,With faltering speech and visage incomposed
, False,,Answered I know thee stranger who thou art
, False,,That mighty leading angel who of late
, False,,Made head against Heavens King though overthrown
, False,,I saw and heard for such a numerous host
, False,,Fled not in silence through the frighted deep
, False,,With ruin upon ruin rout on rout
, False,,Confusion worse confounded and Heavengates
, False,,Poured out by millions her victorious bands
, False,,Pursuing I upon my frontiers here
, False,,Keep residence if all I can will serve
, False,,That little which is left so to defend
, False,,Encroached on still through our intestine broils
, False,,Weakening the scepter of old Night first Hell
, False,,Your dungeon stretching far and wide beneath
, False,,Now lately Heaven and Earth another world
, False,,Hung oer my realm linked in a golden chain
, False,,To that side Heaven from whence your legions fell
, False,,If that way be your walk you have not far
, False,,So much the nearer danger Go and speed
, False,,Havoc and spoil and ruin are my gain
, False,,He ceased and Satan stayed not to reply
, False,,But glad that now his sea should find a shore
, False,,With fresh alacrity and force renewed
, False,,Springs upward like a pyramid of fire
, False,,Into the wild expanse and through the shock
, False,,Of fighting elements on all sides round
, False,,Environed wins his way harder beset
, False,,And more endangered than when Argo passed
, False,,Through Bosporus betwixt the jostling rocks
, False,,Or when Ulysses on the larboard shunned
, False,,Charybdis and by the other whirlpool steered
, False,,So he with difficulty and labor hard
, False,,Moved on with difficulty and labor he
, False,,But he once passed soon after when man fell
, False,,Strange alteration Sin and Death amain
, False,,Following his track such was the will of Heaven
, False,,Paved after him a broad and beaten way
, False,,Over the dark abyss whose boiling gulf
, False,,Tamely endured a bridge of wondrous length
, False,,From Hell continued reaching the utmost orb
, False,,Of this frail world by which the spirits perverse
, False,,With easy intercourse pass to and fro
, False,,To tempt or punish mortals except whom
, False,,God and good angels guard by special grace
, False,,But now at last the sacred influence
, False,,Of light appears and from the walls of Heaven
, False,,Shoots far into the bosom of dim night
, False,,A glimmering dawn Here nature first begins
, False,,Her farthest verge and chaos to retire
, False,,As from her outmost works a broken foe
, False,,With tumult less and with less hostile din
, False,,That Satan with less toil and now with ease
, False,,Wafts on the calmer wave by dubious light
, False,,And like a weatherbeaten vessel holds
, False,,Gladly the port though shrouds and tackle torn
, False,,Or in the emptier waste resembling air
, False,,Weighs his spread wings at leisure to behold
, False,,Far off the empyreal Heaven extended wide
, False,,In circuit undetermined square or round
, False,,With opal towers and battlements adorned
, False,,Of living sapphire once his native seat
, False,,And fast by hanging in a golden chain
, False,,This pendent world in bigness as a star
, False,,Of smallest magnitude close by the moon
, False,,Thither full fraught with mischievous revenge
, False,,Accursed and in a cursed hour he hies
, False,,Hail holy Light offspring of Heaven firstborn
, False,,Or of the Eternal coeternal beam
, False,,May I express thee unblamed since God is light
, False,,And never but in unapproached light
, False,,Dwelt from eternity dwelt then in thee
, False,,Bright effluence of bright essence increate
, False,,Or hear’st thou rather pure ethereal stream
, False,,Whose fountain who shall tell before the sun
, False,,Before the Heavens thou wert and at the voice
, False,,Of God as with a mantle didst invest
, False,,The rising world of waters dark and deep
, False,,Won from the void and formless infinite
, False,,Thee I revisit now with bolder wing
, False,,Escaped the Stygian pool though long detained
, False,,In that obscure sojourn while in my flight
, False,,Through utter and through middle darkness borne
, False,,With other notes than to the Orphean lyre
, False,,I sung of Chaos and eternal Night
, False,,Taught by the heavenly Muse to venture down
, False,,The dark descent and up to reascend
, False,,Though hard and rare Thee I revisit safe
, False,,And feel thy sovereign vital lamp but thou
, False,,Revisitst not these eyes that roll in vain
, False,,To find thy piercing ray and find no dawn
, False,,So thick a drop serene hath quenched their orbs
, False,,Or dim suffusion veiled Yet not the more
, False,,Cease I to wander where the Muses haunt
, False,,Clear spring or shady grove or sunny hill
, False,,Smit with the love of sacred song but chief
, False,,Thee Sion and the flowery brooks beneath
, False,,That wash thy hallowed feet and warbling flow
, False,,Nightly I visit nor sometimes forget
, False,,So were I equaled with them in renown
, False,,Thy sovereign command that man should find grace
, False,,Blind Thamyris and blind Maeonides
, False,,And Tiresias and Phineus prophets old
, False,,Then feed on thoughts that voluntary move
, False,,Harmonious numbers as the wakeful bird
, False,,Sings darkling and in shadiest covert hid
, False,,Tunes her nocturnal note Thus with the year
, False,,Seasons return but not to me returns
, False,,Day or the sweet approach of even or morn
, False,,Or sight of vernal bloom or summers rose
, False,,Or flocks or herds or human face divine
, False,,But cloud instead and everduring dark
, False,,Surrounds me from the cheerful ways of men
, False,,Cut off and for the  of knowledge fair
, False,,Presented with a universal blank
, False,,Of natures works to me expunged and rased
, False,,And wisdom at one entrance quite shut out
, False,,So much the rather thou celestial Light
, False,,Shine inward and the mind through all her powers
, False,,Irradiate there plant eyes all mist from thence
, False,,Purge and disperse that I may see and tell
, False,,Of things invisible to mortal sight
, False,,Now had the Almighty Father from above
, False,,From the pure empyrean where he sits
, False,,High throned above all heighth bent down his eye
, False,,His own works and their works at once to view

, False,,Our two first parents yet the only two
, False,,Of mankind in the happy garden placed

, False,,In blissful solitude he then surveyed

, False,,Wherein past present future he beholds

, False,,Only begotten Son seest thou what rage
, False,,Transports our Adversary whom no bounds

, False,,Upon his own rebellious head And now

, False,,Not far off Heaven in the precincts of light

, False,,And man there placed with purpose to assay
, False,,If him by force he can destroy or worse

, False,,For man will hearken to his glozing lies
, False,,And easily transgress the sole command

, False,,When will and reason reason also is choice
, False,,Useless and vain of freedom both despoiled
, False,,Made passive both had served necessity
, False,,Not me they therefore as to right belonged

, False,,By him corrupted or wilt thou thyself

, False,,Some I have chosen of peculiar grace
, False,,Elect above the rest so is my will
, False,,The rest shall hear me call and oft be warned

, False,,To pray repent and bring obedience due

, False,,Though but endeavored with sincere intent

, False,,They who neglect and scorn shall never taste

, False,,And none but such from mercy I exclude
, False,,But yet all is not done man disobeying
, False,,Disloyal breaks his fealty and sins
, False,,Against the high supremacy of Heaven
, False,,Affecting Godhead and so losing all
, False,,To expiate his treason hath naught left
, False,,But to destruction sacred and devote
, False,,He with his whole posterity must die
, False,,Die he or justice must unless for him
, False,,Some other able and as willing pay
, False,,The rigid satisfaction death for death
, False,,Say heavenly Powers where shall we find such love
, False,,Which of you will be mortal to redeem
, False,,Mans mortal crime and just the unjust to save
, False,,Dwells in all Heaven charity so dear
, False,,And silence was in Heaven on mans behalf
, False,,He asked but all the heavenly quire stood mute
, False,,Patron or intercessor none appeared
, False,,Much less that durst upon his own head draw

, False,,By doom severe had not the Son of God

, False,,His dearest mediation thus renewed

, False,,And shall grace not find means that finds her way
