, False,,Me some inferior angel I had stood
, False,,Then happy no unbounded hope had raised
, False,,Ambition Yet why not some other Power
, False,,As great might have aspired and me though mean
, False,,Drawn to his part but other Powers as great
, False,,Fell not but stand unshaken from within
, False,,Or from without to all temptations armed
, False,,Hadst thou the same free will and power to stand
, False,,Thou hadst whom hast thou then or what to accuse
, False,,But Heavens free love dealt equally to all
, False,,Be then his love accursed since love or hate
, False,,To me alike it deals eternal woe
, False,,Nay cursed be thou since against his thy will
, False,,Chose freely what it now so justly rues
, False,,Me miserable which way shall I fly
, False,,Infinite wrath and infinite despair
, False,,Which way I fly is Hell myself am Hell
, False,,And in the lowest deep a lower deep
, False,,Still threatening to devour me opens wide
, False,,To which the Hell I suffer seems a Heaven
, False,,Oh then at last relent Is there no place
, False,,Left for repentance none for pardon left
, False,,None left but by submission and that word
, False,,Disdain forbids me and my dread of shame
, False,,Among the Spirits beneath whom I seduced
, False,,With other promises and other vaunts
, False,,Than to submit boasting I could subdue
, False,,The Omnipotent Ay me they little know
, False,,How dearly I abide that boast so vain
, False,,Under what torments inwardly I groan
, False,,While they adore me on the throne of Hell
, False,,With diadem and scepter high advanced
, False,,The lower still I fall only supreme
, False,,In misery Such joy ambition finds
, False,,But say I could repent and could obtain
, False,,By act of grace my former state how soon
, False,,Would heighth recall high thoughts how soon unsay
, False,,What feigned submission swore Ease would recant
, False,,Vows made in pain as violent and void
, False,,For never can true reconcilement grow
, False,,Where wounds of deadly hate have pierced so deep
, False,,Which would but lead me to a worse relapse
, False,,And heavier fall so should I purchase dear
, False,,Short intermission bought with double smart
, False,,This knows my Punisher therefore as far
, False,,From granting he as I from begging peace
, False,,All hope excluded thus behold in stead
, False,,Mankind created and for him this world
, False,,So farewell hope and with hope farewell fear
, False,,Farewell remorse all good to me is lost
, False,,Evil be thou my good by thee at least
, False,,Divided empire with Heavens King I hold
, False,,By thee and more than half perhaps will reign
, False,,As man ere long and this new world shall know
, False,,Thus while he spake each passion dimmed his face
, False,,Thrice changed with pale ire envy and despair
, False,,Which marred his borrowed visage and betrayed
, False,,Him counterfeit if any eye beheld
, False,,For heavenly minds from such distempers foul
, False,,Are ever clear Whereof he soon aware
, False,,Each perturbation smoothed with outward calm
, False,,Artificer of fraud and was the first
, False,,That practiced falsehood under saintly show
, False,,Deep malice to conceal couched with revenge
, False,,Yet not enough had practiced to deceive
, False,,Uriel once warned whose eye pursued him down
, False,,The way he went and on the Assyrian mount
, False,,Saw him disfigured more than could befall
, False,,Spirit of happy sort his gestures fierce
, False,,He marked and mad demeanor then alone
, False,,As he supposed all unobserved unseen
, False,,So on he fares and to the border comes
, False,,Of Eden where delicious Paradise
, False,,Now nearer crowns with her enclosure green
, False,,As with a rural mound the champaign head
, False,,Of a steep wilderness whose hairy sides
, False,,Access denied and overhead upgrew
, False,,Insuperable height of loftiest shade
, False,,Cedar and pine and fir and branching palm
, False,,A sylvan scene and as the ranks ascend
, False,,Shade above shade a woody theatre
, False,,Of stateliest view Yet higher than their tops
, False,,The verdurous wall of Paradise upsprung
, False,,Which to our general sire gave prospect large
, False,,Into his nether empire neighboring round
, False,,And higher than that wall a circling row
, False,,Of goodliest trees loaden with fairest fruit
, False,,Blossoms and fruits at once of golden hue
, False,,Appeared with gay enameled colors mixed
, False,,On which the sun more glad impressed his beams
, False,,Than in fair evening cloud or humid bow
, False,,When God hath showered the earth so lovely seemed
, False,,That landscape And of pure now purer air
, False,,Meets his approach and to the heart inspires
, False,,Vernal delight and joy able to drive
, False,,All sadness but despair Now gentle gales
, False,,Fanning their odoriferous wings dispense
, False,,Native perfumes and whisper whence they stole
, False,,Those balmy spoils As when to them who fail
, False,,Beyond the Cape of Hope and now are past
, False,,Mozambique off at sea northeast winds blow
, False,,Sabean odors from the spicy shore
, False,,Of Araby the blest with such delay
, False,,Well pleased they slack their course and many a league
, False,,Cheered with the grateful smell old Ocean smiles
, False,,So entertained those odorous sweets the Fiend
, False,,Who came their bane though with them better pleased
, False,,Than Asmodeus with the fishy fume
, False,,That drove him though enamored from the spouse
, False,,Of Tobits son and with a vengeance sent
, False,,From Media post to Egypt there fast bound
, False,,Now to the ascent of that steep savage hill
, False,,Satan had journeyed on pensive and slow
, False,,But further way found none so thick entwined
, False,,As one continued brake the undergrowth
, False,,Of shrubs and tangling bushes had perplexed
, False,,All path of man or beast that passed that way
, False,,One gate there only was and that looked east
, False,,On the other side which when the archfelon saw
, False,,Due entrance he disdained and in contempt
, False,,At one flight bound high overleaped all bound
, False,,Of hill or highest wall and sheer within
, False,,Lights on his feet As when a prowling wolf
, False,,Whom hunger drives to seek new haunt for prey
, False,,Watching where shepherds pen their flocks at eve
, False,,In hurdled cotes amid the field secure
, False,,Leaps oer the fence with ease into the fold
, False,,Or as a thief bent to unhoard the cash
, False,,Of some rich burgher whose substantial doors
, False,,Crossbarred and bolted fast fear no assault
, False,,In at the window climbs or oer the tiles
, False,,So clomb this first grand thief into Gods fold
, False,,So since into his church lewd hirelings climb
, False,,Thence up he flew and on the tree of life
, False,,The middle tree and highest there that grew
, False,,Sat like a cormorant yet not true life
, False,,Thereby regained but sat devising death
, False,,To them who lived nor on the virtue thought
, False,,Of that lifegiving plant but only used
, False,,For prospect what well used had been the pledge
, False,,Of immortality So little knows
, False,,Any but God alone to value right
, False,,The good before him but perverts best things
, False,,To worst abuse or to their meanest use
, False,,Beneath him with new wonder now he views
, False,,To all delight of human sense exposed
, False,,In narrow room Natures whole wealth yea more
, False,,A Heaven on Earth For blissful Paradise
, False,,Of God the garden was by him in the east
, False,,Of Eden planted Eden stretched her line
, False,,From Auran eastward to the royal towers
, False,,Of great Seleucia built by Grecian kings
, False,,Of where the sons of Eden long before
, False,,Dwelt in Telassar In this pleasant soil
, False,,His far more pleasant garden God ordained
, False,,Out of the fertile ground he caused to grow
, False,,All trees of noblest kind for sight smell taste
, False,,And all amid them stood the tree of life
, False,,High eminent blooming ambrosial fruit
, False,,Of vegetable gold and next to life
, False,,Our death the tree of knowledge grew fast by
, False,,Knowledge of good bought dear by knowing ill
, False,,Southward through Eden went a river large
, False,,Nor changed his course but through the shaggy hill
, False,,Passed underneath ingulfed for God had thrown
, False,,That mountain as his gardenmould high raised
, False,,Upon the rapid current which through veins
, False,,Of porous earth with kindly thirst updrawn
, False,,Rose a fresh fountain and with many a rill
, False,,Watered the garden thence united fell
, False,,Down the steep glade and met the nether flood
, False,,Which from his darksome passage now appears
, False,,And now divided into four main streams
, False,,Runs diverse wandering many a famous realm
, False,,And country whereof here needs no account
, False,,But rather to tell how if Art could tell
, False,,How from that sapphire fount the crisped brooks
, False,,Rolling on orient pearl and sands of gold
, False,,With mazy error under pendant shades
, False,,Ran nectar visiting each plant and fed
, False,,Flowers worthy of Paradise which not nice Art
, False,,In beds and curious knots but Nature boon
, False,,Poured forth profuse on hill and dale and plain
, False,,Both where the morning sun first warmly smote
, False,,The open field and where the unpierced shade
, False,,Imbrowned the noontide bowers Thus was this place
, False,,A happy rural seat of various view
, False,,Groves whose rich trees wept odorous gums and balm
, False,,Others whose fruit burnished with golden rind
, False,,Hung amiable Hesperian fables true
, False,,If true here only and of delicious taste
, False,,Betwixt them lawns or level downs and flocks
, False,,Grazing the tender herb were interposed
, False,,Or palmy hillock or the flowery lap
, False,,Of some irriguous valley spread her store
, False,,Flowers of all hue and without thorn the rose
, False,,Another side umbrageous grots and caves
, False,,Of cool recess oer which the mantling vine
, False,,Lays forth her purple grape and gently creeps
, False,,Luxuriant mean while murmuring waters fall
, False,,Down the slope hills dispersed or in a lake
, False,,That to the fringed bank with myrtle crowned
, False,,Her crystal mirror holds unite their streams
, False,,The birds their quire apply airs vernal airs
, False,,Breathing the smell of field and grove attune
, False,,The trembling leaves while universal Pan
, False,,Knit with the Graces and the Hours in dance
, False,,Led on the eternal Spring Not that fair field
, False,,Of Enna where Proserpine gathering flowers
, False,,Herself a fairer flower by gloomy Dis
, False,,Was gathered which cost Ceres all that pain
, False,,To seek her through the world nor that sweet grove
, False,,Of Daphne by Orontes and the inspired
, False,,Castalian spring might with this Paradise
, False,,Of Eden strive nor that Nyseian isle
, False,,Girt with the river Triton where old Cham
, False,,Whom Gentiles Ammon call and Libyan Jove
, False,,Hid Amalthea and her florid son
, False,,Young Bacchus from his stepdame Rheas eye
, False,,Nor where Abassin kings their issue guard
, False,,Mount Amara though this by some supposed
, False,,True Paradise under the Ethiop line
, False,,By Nilus head enclosed with shining rock
, False,,A whole days journey high but wide remote
, False,,From this Assyrian garden where the Fiend
, False,,Saw undelighted all delight all kind
, False,,Of living creatures new to sight and strange
, False,,Two of far nobler shape erect and tall
, False,,Godlike erect with native honor clad
, False,,In naked majesty seemed lords of all
, False,,And worthy seemed for in their looks divine
, False,,The image of their glorious Maker shone
, False,,Truth wisdom sanctitude severe and pure
, False,,Severe but in true filial freedom placed
, False,,Whence true authority in men though both
, False,,Not equal as their sex not equal seemed
, False,,For contemplation he and velour formed
, False,,For softness she and sweet attractive grace
, False,,He for God only she for God in him
, False,,His fair large front and eye sublime declared
, False,,Absolute rule and hyacinthine locks
, False,,Round from his parted forelock manly hung
, False,,Clustering but not beneath his shoulders broad
, False,,She as a veil down to the slender waist
, False,,Her unadorned golden tresses wore
, False,,Disheveled but in wanton ringlets waved
, False,,As the vine curls her tendrils which implied
, False,,Subjection but required with gentle sway
, False,,And by her yielded by him best received
, False,,Yielded with coy submission modest pride
, False,,And sweet reluctant amorous delay
, False,,Nor those mysterious parts were then concealed
, False,,Then was not guilty shame dishonest shame
, False,,Of natures works honor dishonorable
, False,,Sinbred how have ye troubled all mankind
, False,,With shows instead mere shows of seeming pure
, False,,And banished from mans life his happiest life
, False,,Simplicity and spotless innocence
, False,,So passed they naked on nor shunned the sight
, False,,Of God or angel for they thought no ill
, False,,So hand in hand they passed the loveliest pair
, False,,That ever since in loves embraces met
, False,,Adam the goodliest man of men since born
, False,,His sons the fairest of her daughters Eve
, False,,Under a tuft of shade that on a green
, False,,Stood whispering soft by a fresh fountain side
, False,,They sat them down and after no more toil
, False,,Of their sweet gardening labor than sufficed
, False,,To recommend cool Zephyr and made ease
, False,,More easy wholesome thirst and appetite
, False,,More grateful to their supperfruits they fell
, False,,Nectarine fruits which the compliant boughs
, False,,Yielded them sidelong as they sat recline
, False,,On the soft downy bank damasked with flowers
, False,,The savory pulp they chew and in the rind
, False,,Still as they thirsted scoop the brimming stream
, False,,Nor gentle purpose nor endearing smiles
, False,,Wanted nor youthful dalliance as beseems
, False,,Fair couple linked in happy nuptial league
, False,,Alone as they About them frisking played
, False,,All beasts of the earth since wild and of all chase
, False,,In wood or wilderness forest or den
, False,,Sporting the lion ramped and in his paw
, False,,Dandled the kid bears tigers ounces pards
, False,,Gamboled before them the unwieldy elephant
, False,,To make them mirth used all his might and wreathed
, False,,His lithe proboscis close the serpent sly
, False,,Insinuating wove with Gordian twine
, False,,His braided train and of his fatal guile
, False,,Gave proof unheeded others on the grass
, False,,Couched and now filled with pasture gazing sat
, False,,Or bedward ruminating for the sun
, False,,Declined was hasting now with prone career
, False,,To the ocean isles and in the ascending scale
, False,,Of Heaven the stars that usher evening rose
, False,,When Satan still in gaze as first he stood
, False,,Scarce thus at length failed speech recovered sad
, False,,Oh Hell what do mine eyes with grief behold
, False,,Into our room of bliss thus high advanced
, False,,Creatures of other mould earthborn perhaps
, False,,Not Spirits yet to heavenly Spirits bright
, False,,Little inferior whom my thoughts pursue
, False,,With wonder and could love so lively shines
, False,,In them divine resemblance and such grace
, False,,The hand that formed them on their shape hath poured
, False,,Ah gentle pair ye little think how nigh
, False,,Your change approaches when all these delights
, False,,Will vanish and deliver ye to woe
, False,,More woe the more your taste is now of joy
, False,,Happy but for so happy ill secured
, False,,Long to continue and this high seat your Heaven
, False,,Ill fenced for Heaven to keep out such a foe
, False,,As now is entered yet no purposed foe
, False,,To you whom I could pity thus forlorn
, False,,Though I unpitied League with you I seek
, False,,And mutual amity so strait so close
, False,,That I with you must dwell or you with me
, False,,Henceforth my dwelling haply may not please
, False,,Like this fair Paradise your sense yet such
, False,,Accept your Makers work he gave it me
, False,,Which I as freely give Hell shall unfold
, False,,To entertain you two her widest gates
, False,,And send forth all her kings there will be room
, False,,Not like these narrow limits to receive
, False,,Your numerous offspring if no better place
, False,,Thank him who puts me loath to this revenge
, False,,On you who wrong me not for him who wronged
, False,,And should I at your harmless innocence
, False,,Melt as I do yet public reason just
, False,,Honor and empire with revenge enlarged
, False,,By conquering this new world compels me now
, False,,To do what else though damned I should abhor
, False,,So spake the Fiend and with necessity
, False,,The tyrants plea excused his devilish deeds
, False,,Then from his lofty stand on that high tree
, False,,Down he alights among the sportful herd
, False,,Of those fourfooted kinds himself now one
, False,,Now other as their shape served best his end
, False,,Nearer to view his prey and unespied
, False,,To mark what of their state he more might learn
, False,,By word or action marked About them round
, False,,A lion now he stalks with fiery glare
, False,,Then as a tiger who by chance hath spied
, False,,In some purlieu two gentle fawns at play
, False,,Straight couches close then rising changes oft
, False,,His couchant watch as one who chose his ground
, False,,Whence rushing he might surest seize them both
, False,,Griped in each paw when Adam first of men
, False,,To first of women Eve thus moving speech
, False,,Turned him all ear to hear new utterance flow
, False,,Sole partner and sole part of all these joys
, False,,Dearer thyself than all needs must the Power
, False,,That made us and for us this ample world
, False,,Be infinitely good and of his good
, False,,As liberal and free as infinite
, False,,That raised us from the dust and placed us here
, False,,In all this happiness who at his hand
, False,,Have nothing merited nor can perform
, False,,Aught whereof he hath need he who requires
, False,,From us no other service than to keep
, False,,This one this easy charge of all the trees
, False,,In Paradise that bear delicious fruit
, False,,So various not to taste that only tree
, False,,Of knowledge planted by the tree of life
, False,,So near grows death to life whateer death is
, False,,Some dreadful thing no doubt for well thou knowest
, False,,God hath pronounced it death to taste that tree
, False,,The only sign of our obedience left
, False,,Among so many signs of power and rule
, False,,Conferred upon us and dominion given
, False,,Over all other creatures that possess
, False,,Earth air and sea Then let us not think hard
, False,,One easy prohibition who enjoy
, False,,Free leave so large to all things else and choice
, False,,Unlimited of manifold delights
, False,,But let us ever praise him and extol
, False,,His bounty following our delightful task
, False,,To prune these growing plants and tend these flowers
, False,,Which were it toilsome yet with thee were sweet
, False,,To whom thus Eve replied Oh thou for whom
, False,,And from whom I was formed flesh of thy flesh
, False,,And without whom am to no end my guide
, False,,And head what thou hast said is just and right
, False,,For we to him indeed all praises owe
, False,,And daily thanks I chiefly who enjoy
, False,,So far the happier lot enjoying thee
, False,,Preeminent by so much odds while thou
, False,,Like consort to thyself canst no where find
, False,,That day I oft remember when from sleep
, False,,I first awaked and found myself reposed
, False,,Under a shade on flowers much wondering where
, False,,And what I was whence thither brought and how
, False,,Not distant far from thence a murmuring sound
, False,,Of waters issued from a cave and spread
, False,,Into a liquid plain then stood unmoved
, False,,Pure as the expanse of Heaven I thither went
, False,,With unexperienced thought and laid me down
, False,,On the green bank to look into the clear
, False,,Smooth lake that to me seemed another sky
, False,,As I bent down to look just opposite
, False,,A shape within the watery gleam appeared
, False,,Bending to look on me I started back
, False,,It started back but pleased I soon returned
, False,,Pleased it returned as soon with answering looks
, False,,Of sympathy and love There I had fixed
, False,,Mine eyes till now and pined with vain desire
, False,,Had not a voice thus warned me What thou seest
, False,,What there thou seest fair Creature is thyself
, False,,With thee it came and goes but follow me
, False,,And I will bring thee where no shadow stays
, False,,Thy coming and thy soft embraces he
, False,,Whose image thou art him thou shalt enjoy
, False,,Inseparably thine to him shalt bear
, False,,Multitudes like thyself and thence be called
, False,,Mother of human race What could I do
, False,,But follow straight invisibly thus led
, False,,Till I espied thee fair indeed and tall
, False,,Under a platane yet methought less fair
, False,,Less winning soft less amiably mild
, False,,Than that smooth watery image Back I turned
, False,,Thou following cried’st aloud Return fair Eve
, False,,Whom flyest thou whom thou flyest of him thou art
, False,,His flesh his bone to give thee being I lent
, False,,Out of my side to thee nearest my heart
, False,,Substantial life to have thee by my side
, False,,Henceforth an individual solace dear
, False,,Part of my soul I seek thee and thee claim
, False,,My other half With that thy gentle hand
, False,,Seized mine I yielded and from that time see
, False,,How beauty is excelled by manly grace
, False,,And wisdom which alone is truly fair
, False,,So spake our general mother and with eyes
, False,,Of conjugal attraction unreproved
, False,,And meek surrender halfembracing leaned
, False,,On our first father half her swelling breast
, False,,Naked met his under the flowing gold
, False,,Of her loose tresses hid he in delight
, False,,Both of her beauty and submissive charms
, False,,Smiled with superior love as Jupiter
, False,,On Juno smiles when he impregns the clouds
, False,,That shed Mayflowers and pressed her matron lip
, False,,With kisses pure Aside the Devil turned
, False,,For envy yet with jealous leer malign
, False,,Eyed them askance and to himself thus ‘plained
, False,,Sight hateful sight tormenting thus these two
, False,,Imparadised in one anothers arms
, False,,The happier Eden shall enjoy their fill
, False,,Of bliss on bliss while I to Hell am thrust
, False,,Where neither joy nor love but fierce desire
, False,,Among our other torments not the least
, False,,Still unfulfilled with pain of longing pines
, False,,Yet let me not forget what I have gained
, False,,From their own mouths All is not theirs it seems
, False,,One fatal tree there stands of knowledge called
, False,,Forbidden them to taste Knowledge forbidden
, False,,Suspicious reasonless Why should their Lord
, False,,Envy them that Can it be sin to know
, False,,Can it be death And do they only stand
, False,,By ignorance Is that their happy state
, False,,The proof of their obedience and their faith
, False,,Oh fair foundation laid whereon to build
, False,,Their ruin hence I will excite their minds
, False,,With more desire to know and to reject
, False,,Envious commands invented with design
, False,,To keep them low whom knowledge might exalt
, False,,Equal with Gods aspiring to be such

, False,,Some wandering Spirit of Heaven by fountain side

, False,,Yet happy pair enjoy till I return
, False,,Short pleasures for long woes are to succeed
, False,,So saying his proud step he scornful turned
, False,,But with sly circumspection and began

, False,,Mean while in utmost longitude where Heaven
, False,,With earth and ocean meets the setting sun
, False,,Slowly descended and with right aspect
, False,,Against the eastern gate of Paradise
, False,,Leveled his evening rays It was a rock
, False,,Of alabaster piled up to the clouds
, False,,Conspicuous far winding with one ascent
, False,,Accessible from earth one entrance high
, False,,The rest was craggy cliff that overhung
, False,,Still as it rose impossible to climb
, False,,Betwixt these rocky pillars Gabriel sat
, False,,Chief of the angelic guards awaiting night
, False,,About him exercised heroic games
, False,,The unarmed youth of Heaven but nigh at hand
, False,,Celestial armory shields helms and spears
, False,,Hung high with diamond flaming and with gold

, False,,In autumn thwarts the night when vapors fired
, False,,Impress the air and shows the mariner
, False,,From what point of his compass to beware
, False,,Impetuous winds He thus began in haste
, False,,Gabriel to thee thy course by lot hath given
, False,,Charge and strict watch that to this happy place
, False,,No evil thing approach or enter in
, False,,This day at heighth of noon came to my sphere
, False,,A Spirit zealous as he seemed to know
, False,,More of the Almightys works and chiefly Man
, False,,Gods latest image I described his way
, False,,Bent all on speed and marked his aerie gait
, False,,But in the mount that lies from Eden north
, False,,Where he first lighted soon discerned his looks
, False,,Alien from Heaven with passions foul obscured
, False,,Mine eye pursued him still but under shade
, False,,Lost sight of him One of the banished crew
, False,,I fear hath ventured from the deep to raise
, False,,New troubles him thy care must be to find
, False,,To whom the winged warrior thus returned
, False,,Uriel no wonder if thy perfect sight
, False,,Amid the suns bright circle where thou sits
, False,,See far and wide In at this gate none pass
, False,,The vigilance here placed but such as come
, False,,Well known from Heaven and since meridian hour
, False,,No creature thence If spirit of other sort
, False,,So minded have oerleaped these earthly bounds
, False,,On purpose hard thou knowest it to exclude
, False,,Spiritual substance with corporeal bar
, False,,But if within the circuit of these walks
, False,,In whatsoever shape he lurk of whom
, False,,Thou tellest by morrow dawning I shall know
, False,,So promised he and Uriel to his charge
, False,,Returned on that bright beam whose point now raised
, False,,Bore him slope downward to the sun now fallen
, False,,Beneath the Azores whether the prime orb
, False,,Incredible how swift had thither rolled
, False,,Diurnal or this less voluble earth
, False,,By shorter flight to the east had left him there
, False,,Arraying with reflected purple and gold
, False,,The clouds that on his western throne attend

, False,,Had in her sober livery all things clad
, False,,Silence accompanied for beast and bird
, False,,They to their grassy couch these to their nests
, False,,Were slunk all but the wakeful nightingale
, False,,She all night long her amorous descant sung
, False,,Silence was pleased Now glowed the firmament
, False,,With living sapphires Hesperus that led
, False,,The starry host rode brightest till the moon
, False,,Rising in clouded majesty at length
, False,,Apparent queen unveiled her peerless light
, False,,And oer the dark her silver mantle threw
, False,,When Adam thus to Eve Fair Consort the hour
, False,,Of night and all things now retired to rest
, False,,Mind us of like repose since God hath set
, False,,Labor and rest as day and night to men
, False,,Successive and the timely dew of sleep
, False,,Now falling with soft slumberous weight inclines
, False,,Our eyelids Other creatures all day long
, False,,Rove idle unemployed and less need rest
, False,,Man hath his daily work of body or mind
, False,,Appointed which declares his dignity
, False,,And the regard of Heaven on all his ways
, False,,While other animals unactive range
, False,,And of their doings God takes no account
, False,,Tomorrow ere fresh morning streak the east
, False,,With first approach of light we must be risen
, False,,And at our pleasant labor to reform
, False,,Yon flowery arbors yonder alleys green
, False,,Our walk at noon with branches overgrown
, False,,That mock our scant manuring and require
, False,,More hands than ours to lop their wanton growth
, False,,Those blossoms also and those dropping gums
, False,,That lie bestrewn unsightly and unsmooth
, False,,Ask riddance if we mean to tread with ease
, False,,Mean while as Nature wills night bids us rest
, False,,To whom thus Eve with perfect beauty adorned
, False,,My Author and Disposer what thou bidst
, False,,Unargued I obey So God ordains
, False,,God is thy law thou mine To know no more
, False,,Is womans happiest knowledge and her praise
, False,,With thee conversing I forget all time
, False,,All seasons and their change all please alike
, False,,Sweet is the breath of Morn her rising sweet
, False,,With charm of earliest birds pleasant the sun
, False,,When first on this delightful land he spreads
, False,,His orient beams on herb tree fruit and flower
, False,,Glistering with dew fragrant the fertile earth
, False,,After soft showers and sweet the coming on
, False,,Of grateful Evening mild then silent Night
, False,,With this her solemn bird and this fair moon
, False,,And these the gems of Heaven her starry train
, False,,But neither breath of Morn when she ascends
, False,,With charm of earliest birds nor rising sun
, False,,On this delightful land nor herb fruit flower
, False,,Glistering with dew nor fragrance after showers
, False,,Nor grateful Evening mild nor silent Night
, False,,With this her solemn bird nor walk by moon
, False,,Or glittering starlight without thee is sweet
, False,,But wherefore all night long shine these for whom
, False,,This glorious sight when sleep hath shut all eyes
, False,,To whom our general ancestor replied
, False,,Daughter of God and Man accomplished Eve
, False,,These have their course to finish round the earth
, False,,By morrow evening and from land to land
, False,,In order though to nations yet unborn
, False,,Ministering light prepared they set and rise
, False,,Lest total Darkness should by night regain
, False,,Her old possession and extinguish life
, False,,In Nature and all things which these soft fires
, False,,Not only enlighten but with kindly heat
, False,,Of various influence foment and warm
, False,,Temper or nourish or in part shed down
, False,,Their stellar virtue on all kinds that grow
, False,,On earth made hereby apter to receive
, False,,Perfection from the suns more potent ray
, False,,These then though unbeheld in deep of night
, False,,Shine not in vain nor think though men were none
, False,,That Heaven would want spectators God want praise
, False,,Millions of spiritual creatures walk the earth
, False,,Unseen both when we wake and when we sleep
, False,,All these with ceaseless praise his works behold
, False,,Both day and night How often from the steep
, False,,Of echoing hill or thicket have we heard
, False,,Celestial voices to the midnight air
, False,,Sole or responsive each to others note
, False,,Singing their great Creator oft in bands
, False,,While they keep watch or nightly rounding walk
, False,,With heavenly touch of instrumental sounds
, False,,In full harmonic number joined their songs
, False,,Divide the night and lift our thoughts to Heaven
, False,,Thus talking hand in hand alone they passed
, False,,On to their blissful bower it was a place
, False,,Chosen by the sovereign Planter when he framed
, False,,All things to Mans delightful use the roof
, False,,Of thickest covert was inwoven shade
, False,,Laurel and myrtle and what higher grew
, False,,Of firm and fragrant leaf on either side
, False,,Acanthus and each odorous bushy shrub
, False,,Fenced up the verdant wall each beauteous flower
, False,,Iris all hues roses and jessamine
, False,,Reared high their flourished heads between and wrought
, False,,Mosaic underfoot the violet
, False,,Crocus and hyacinth with rich inlay
, False,,Broidered the ground more colored than with stone
, False,,Of costliest emblem Other creature here
, False,,Bird beast insect or worm durst enter none
, False,,Such was their awe of Man In shadier bower
, False,,More sacred and sequestered though but feigned
, False,,Pan or Sylvanus never slept nor Nymph
, False,,Nor Faunus haunted Here in close recess
, False,,With flowers garlands and sweetsmelling herbs
, False,,Espoused Eve decked first her nuptial bed
, False,,And heavenly quires the hymenaean sung
, False,,What day the genial angel to our sire
, False,,Brought her in naked beauty more adorned
, False,,More lovely than Pandora whom the Gods
, False,,Endowed with all their gifts and O too like
, False,,In sad event when to the unwiser son
, False,,Of Japhet brought by Hermes she ensnared
, False,,Mankind with her fair looks to be avenged
, False,,On him who had stole Joves authentic fire
, False,,Thus at their shady lodge arrived both stood
, False,,Both turned and under open sky adored
, False,,The God that made both sky air earth and heaven
, False,,Which they beheld the moons resplendent globe
, False,,And starry pole Thou also madest the night
, False,,Maker Omnipotent and thou the day
, False,,Which we in our appointed work employed
, False,,Have finished happy in our mutual help
, False,,And mutual love the crown of all our bliss
, False,,Ordained by thee and this delicious place
, False,,For us too large where thy abundance wants
, False,,Partakers and uncropped falls to the ground
, False,,But thou hast promised from us two a race
, False,,To fill the earth who shall with us extol
, False,,Thy goodness infinite both when we wake
, False,,And when we seek as now thy gift of sleep
, False,,This said unanimous and other rites
, False,,Observing none but adoration pure
, False,,Which God likes best into their inmost bower
, False,,Handed they went and eased the putting off
, False,,These troublesome disguises which we wear
, False,,Straight side by side were laid nor turned I ween
, False,,Adam from his fair spouse nor Eve the rites
, False,,Mysterious of connubial love refused
, False,,Whatever hypocrites austerely talk
, False,,Of purity and place and innocence
, False,,Defaming as impure what God declares
, False,,Pure and commands to some leaves free to all
, False,,Our Maker bids increase who bids abstain
, False,,But our Destroyer foe to God and Man
, False,,Hail wedded Love mysterious law true source
, False,,Of human offspring sole propriety
, False,,In Paradise of all things common else
, False,,By thee adulterous Lust was driven from men
, False,,Among the bestial herds to range by thee
, False,,Founded in reason loyal just and pure
, False,,Relations dear and all the charities
, False,,Of father son and brother first were known
, False,,Far be it that I should write thee sin or blame
, False,,Or think thee unbefitting holiest place
, False,,Perpetual fountain of domestic sweets
, False,,Whose bed is undefiled and chaste pronounced
, False,,Present or past as saints and patriarchs used
, False,,Here Love his golden shafts employs here lights
, False,,His constant lamp and waves his purple wings
, False,,Reigns here and revels not in the bought smile
, False,,Of harlots loveless joyless unendeared
, False,,Casual fruition nor in courtamours
, False,,Mixed dance or wanton mask or midnight ball
, False,,Or serenade which the starved lover sings
, False,,To his proud fair best quitted with disdain
, False,,These lulled by nightingales embracing slept
, False,,And on their naked limbs the flowery roof
, False,,Showered roses which the morn repaired Sleep on
, False,,Blest pair and Oh yet happiest if ye seek
, False,,No happier state and know to know no more
, False,,Now had night measured with her shadowy cone
, False,,Half way up hill this vast sublunar vault
, False,,And from their ivory port the Cherubim
, False,,Forth issuing at the accustomed hour stood armed
, False,,To their night watches in warlike parade
, False,,When Gabriel to his next in power thus spake
, False,,Uzziel half these draw off and coast the south
, False,,With strictest watch these other wheel the north
, False,,Our circuit meets full west As flame they part
, False,,Half wheeling to the shield half to the spear
, False,,From these two strong and subtle Spirits he called
, False,,That near him stood and gave them thus in charge
, False,,Ithuriel and Zephon with winged speed
, False,,Search through this garden leave unsearched no nook
, False,,But chiefly where those two fair creatures lodge
, False,,Now laid perhaps asleep secure of harm
, False,,This evening from the suns decline arrived
, False,,Who tells of some infernal Spirit seen
, False,,Hitherward bent who could have thought escaped
, False,,The bars of Hell on errand bad no doubt
, False,,Such where ye find seize fast and hither bring
, False,,So saying on he led his radiant files
, False,,Dazzling the moon these to the bower direct
, False,,In search of whom they sought Him there they found
, False,,Squat like a toad close at the ear of Eve
, False,,Assaying by his devilish art to reach
, False,,The organs of her fancy and with them forge
, False,,Illusions as he list phantasms and dreams
, False,,Or if inspiring venom he might taint
, False,,The animal spirits that from pure blood arise
, False,,Like gentle breaths from rivers pure thence raise
, False,,At least distempered discontented thoughts
, False,,Vain hopes vain aims inordinate desires
, False,,Blown up with high conceits ingendering pride
, False,,Him thus intent Ithuriel with his spear
, False,,Touched lightly for no falsehood can endure
, False,,Touch of celestial temper but returns
, False,,Of force to its own likeness Up he starts
, False,,Discovered and surprised As when a spark
, False,,Lights on a heap of nitrous powder laid
, False,,Fit for the tun some magazine to store
, False,,Against a rumored war the smutty grain
, False,,With sudden blaze diffused inflames the air
, False,,So started up in his own shape the Fiend
, False,,Back stepped those two fair angels half amazed
, False,,So sudden to behold the grisly king
, False,,Yet thus unmoved with fear accost him soon
, False,,Which of those rebel Spirits adjudged to Hell
, False,,Comest thou escaped thy prison and transformed
, False,,Why satst thou like an enemy in wait
, False,,Here watching at the head of these that sleep
, False,,Know ye not then said Satan filled with scorn
, False,,Know ye not me ye knew me once no mate
, False,,For you there sitting where ye durst not soar
, False,,Not to know me argues yourselves unknown
, False,,The lowest of your throng or if ye know
, False,,Why ask ye and superfluous begin
, False,,Your message like to end as much in vain
, False,,To whom thus Zephon answering scorn with scorn
, False,,Think not revolted spirit thy shape the same
, False,,Or undiminished brightness to be known
, False,,As when thou stoodest in Heaven upright and pure
, False,,That glory then when thou no more wast good
, False,,Departed from thee and thou resemblest now
, False,,Thy sin and place of doom obscure and foul
, False,,But come for thou be sure shalt give account
, False,,To him who sent us whose charge is to keep
, False,,This place inviolable and these from harm
, False,,So spake the Cherub and his grave rebuke
, False,,Severe in youthful beauty added grace
, False,,Invincible Abashed the devil stood
, False,,And felt how awful goodness is and saw
, False,,Virtue in her shape how lovely saw and pined
, False,,His loss but chiefly to find here observed
, False,,His luster visibly impaired yet seemed
, False,,Undaunted If I must contend said he
, False,,Best with the best the sender not the sent
, False,,Or all at once more glory will be won
, False,,Or less be lost Thy fear said Zephon bold
, False,,Will save us trial what the least can do
, False,,Single against thee wicked and thence weak
, False,,The Fiend replied not overcome with rage
, False,,But like a proud steed reined went haughty on
, False,,Champing his iron curb To strive or fly
, False,,He held it vain awe from above had quelled
, False,,His heart not else dismayed Now drew they nigh
, False,,The western point where those halfrounding guards
, False,,Just met and closing stood in squadron joined
, False,,A waiting next command To whom their Chief
, False,,Gabriel from the front thus called aloud
, False,,Oh friends I hear the tread of nimble feet
, False,,Hasting this way and now by glimpse discern
, False,,Ithuriel and Zephon through the shade
, False,,And with them comes a third of regal port
, False,,But faded splendor wan who by his gait
, False,,And fierce demeanor seems the Prince of Hell
, False,,Not likely to part hence without contest
, False,,Stand firm for in his look defiance lours
, False,,He scarce had ended when those two approached
, False,,And brief related whom they brought where found
, False,,How busied in what form and posture couched
, False,,To whom with stern regard thus Gabriel spake
, False,,Why hast thou Satan broke the bounds prescribed
, False,,To thy transgressions and disturbed the charge
, False,,Of others who approve not to transgress
, False,,By thy example but have power and right
, False,,To question thy bold entrance on this place
, False,,Employed it seems to violate sleep and those
, False,,Whose dwelling God hath planted here in bliss
, False,,To whom thus Satan with contemptuous brow
, False,,Gabriel thou hadst in Heaven the esteem of wise
, False,,And such I held thee but this question asked
, False,,Puts me in doubt Lives there who loves his pain
, False,,Who would not finding way break loose from Hell
, False,,Though thither doomed Thou wouldst thyself no doubt
, False,,And boldly venture to whatever place
, False,,Farthest from pain where thou mightst hope to change
, False,,Torment with ease and soonest recompense
, False,,Dole with delight which in this place I sought
, False,,To thee no reason who knowest only good
, False,,But evil hast not tried and wilt object
, False,,His will who bounds us Let him surer bar
, False,,His iron gates if he intends our stay
, False,,In that dark durance Thus much what was asked
, False,,The rest is true they found me where they say
, False,,But that implies not violence or harm
, False,,Thus he in scorn The warlike angel moved
, False,,Disdainfully half smiling thus replied
, False,,Oh loss of one in Heaven to judge of wise
, False,,Since Satan fell whom folly overthrew
, False,,And now returns him from his prison scaped
, False,,Gravely in doubt whether to hold them wise
, False,,Or not who ask what boldness brought him hither
, False,,Unlicensed from his bounds in Hell prescribed
, False,,So wise he judges it to fly from pain
, False,,However and to scape his punishment
, False,,So judge thou still presumptuous till the wrath
, False,,Which thou incurrest by flying meet thy flight
, False,,Sevenfold and scourge that wisdom back to Hell
, False,,Which taught thee yet no better that no pain
, False,,Can equal anger infinite provoked
, False,,But wherefore thou alone wherefore with thee
, False,,Came not all hell broke loose or thou than they
, False,,Less hardy to endure Courageous Chief
, False,,The first in flight from pain hadst thou alleged
, False,,To thy deserted host this cause of flight
, False,,Thou surely hadst not come sole fugitive
, False,,To which the fiend thus answered frowning stern
, False,,Not that I less endure or shrink from pain
, False,,Insulting angel well thou knowest I stood
, False,,Thy fiercest when in battle to thy aid
, False,,The blasting volleyed thunder made all speed
, False,,And seconded thy else not dreaded spear
, False,,But still thy words at random as before
, False,,Argue thy inexperience what behooves
, False,,From hard assays and ill successes past
, False,,A faithful leader not to hazard all
, False,,Through ways of danger by himself untried
, False,,I therefore I alone first undertook
, False,,To wing the desolate abyss and spy
, False,,This new created world whereof in Hell
, False,,Fame is not silent here in hope to find
, False,,Better abode and my afflicted Powers
, False,,To settle here on earth or in mid air
, False,,Though for possession put to try once more
, False,,What thou and thy gay legions dare against
, False,,Whose easier business were to serve their Lord
, False,,High up in Heaven with songs to hymn his throne
, False,,And practiced distances to cringe not fight
, False,,To whom the warrior angel soon replied
, False,,To say and straight unsay pretending first
, False,,Wise to fly pain professing next the spy
, False,,Argues no leader but a liar traced
, False,,Satan and couldst thou faithful add Oh name
, False,,Oh sacred name of faithfulness profaned
, False,,Faithful to whom to thy rebellious crew
, False,,Army of Fiends fit body to fit head
, False,,Was this your discipline and faith engaged
, False,,Your military obedience to dissolve
, False,,Allegiance to the acknowledged Power supreme
, False,,And thou sly hypocrite who now wouldst seem
, False,,Patron of liberty who more than thou
, False,,Once fawned and cringed and servilely adored
, False,,Heavens awful Monarch wherefore but in hope
, False,,To dispossess him and thyself to reign
, False,,But mark what I areed thee now Avaunt
, False,,Fly neither whence thou fledst If from this hour
, False,,Within these hallowed limits thou appear
, False,,Back to the infernal pit I drag thee chained
, False,,And seal thee so as henceforth not to scorn
, False,,The facile gates of Hell too slightly barred
, False,,So threatened he but Satan to no threats
, False,,Gave heed but wang more in rage replied
, False,,Then when I am thy captive talk of chains
, False,,Proud limitary Cherub but ere then
, False,,Far heavier load thyself expect to feel
, False,,From my prevailing arm though Heavens King
, False,,Ride on thy wings and thou with thy compeers
, False,,Used to the yoke drawest his triumphant wheels
, False,,In progress through the road of Heaven starpaved
, False,,While thus he spake the angelic squadron bright

, False,,Their phalanx and began to hem him round
, False,,With ported spears as thick as when a field
, False,,Of Ceres ripe for harvest waving bends
, False,,Her bearded grove of ears which way the wind
, False,,Sways them the careful plowman doubting stands
, False,,Left on the threshing floor his hopeless sheaves
, False,,Prove chaff On the other side Satan alarmed
, False,,Collecting all his might dilated stood
, False,,Like Tenerife or Atlas unremoved
, False,,His stature reached the sky and on his crest
, False,,Sat Horror plumed nor wanted in his grasp
, False,,What seemed both spear and shield Now dreadful deeds
, False,,Might have ensued nor only Paradise
, False,,In this commotion but the starry cope
, False,,Of Heaven perhaps or all the elements
, False,,At least had gone to wrack disturbed and torn
, False,,With violence of this conflict had not soon
, False,,The Eternal to prevent such horrid fray
, False,,Hung forth in Heaven his golden scales yet seen
, False,,Betwixt Astraea and the Scorpion sign
, False,,Wherein all things created first he weighed
, False,,The pendulous round earth with balanced air
, False,,In counterpoise now ponders all events
, False,,Battles and realms In these he put two weights
, False,,The sequel each of parting and of fight
, False,,The latter quick up flew and kicked the beam
, False,,Which Gabriel spying thus bespake the Fiend
, False,,Satan I know thy strength and thou knowest mine
, False,,Neither our own but given What folly then
, False,,To boast what arms can do since thine no more
, False,,Than Heaven permits nor mine though doubled now
, False,,To trample thee as mire For proof look up
, False,,And read thy lot in yon celestial sign
, False,,Where thou art weighed and shown how light how weak
, False,,If thou resist The Fiend looked up and knew
, False,,His mounted scale aloft Nor more but fled
, False,,Murmuring and with him fled the shades of night
, False,,Now Morn her rosy steps in the eastern clime
, False,,Advancing sowed the earth with orient pearl
, False,,When Adam waked so customed for his sleep
, False,,Was aerielight from pure digestion bred
, False,,And temperate vapors bland which the only sound
, False,,Of leaves and fuming rills Auroras fan
, False,,Lightly dispersed and the shrill matin song
, False,,Of birds on every bough so much the more
, False,,His wonder was to find unwakened Eve
, False,,With tresses discomposed and glowing cheek
, False,,As through unquiet rest He on his side
, False,,Leaning half raised with looks of cordial love
, False,,Hung over her enamored and beheld
, False,,Beauty which whether waking or asleep
, False,,Shot forth peculiar graces then with voice
, False,,Mild as when Zephyrus on Flora breathes
, False,,Her hand soft touching whispered thus Awake
, False,,My fairest my espoused my latest found
, False,,Heavens last best gift my ever new delight
, False,,Awake The morning shines and the fresh field
, False,,Calls us we lose the prime to mark how spring
, False,,Our tender plants how blows the citron grove
, False,,What drops the myrrh and what the balmy reed
, False,,How nature paints her colors how the bee
, False,,Sits on the bloom extracting liquid sweet
, False,,Such whispering waked her but with startled eye
, False,,On Adam whom embracing thus she spake
, False,,Oh sole in whom my thoughts find all repose
, False,,My glory my perfection glad I see
, False,,Thy face and morn returned for I this night
, False,,Such night till this I never passed have dreamed
, False,,If dreamed not as I oft am wont of thee
, False,,Works of day past or morrows next design
, False,,But of offence and trouble which my mind
, False,,Knew never till this irksome night Methought
, False,,Close at mine ear one called me forth to walk
, False,,With gentle voice I thought it thine It said
, False,,Why sleepest thou Eve now is the pleasant time
, False,,The cool the silent save where silence yields
, False,,To the nightwarbling bird that now awake
, False,,Tunes sweetest his lovelabored song now reigns
, False,,Fullorbed the moon and with more pleasing light
, False,,Shadowy sets off the face of things in vain
, False,,If none regard Heaven wakes with all his eyes
, False,,Whom to behold but thee Natures desire
, False,,In whose sight all things joy with ravishment
, False,,Attracted by thy beauty still to gaze
, False,,I rose as at thy call but found thee not
, False,,To find thee I directed then my walk
, False,,And on methought alone I passed through ways
, False,,That brought me on a sudden to the tree
, False,,Of interdicted knowledge fair it seemed
, False,,Much fairer to my fancy than by day
, False,,And as I wondering looked beside it stood
, False,,One shaped and winged like one of those from Heaven
, False,,By us oft seen his dewy locks distilled
, False,,Ambrosia on that tree he also gazed
, False,,And O fair plant said he with fruit surcharged
, False,,edeigns none to ease thy load and taste thy sweet
, False,,Nor God nor Man Is knowledge so despised
, False,,Or envy or what reserve forbids to taste
, False,,Forbid who will none shall from me withhold
, False,,Longer thy offered good why else set here
, False,,This said he paused not but with venturous arm
, False,,He plucked he tasted me damp horror chilled
, False,,At such bold words vouched with a deed so bold
, False,,But he thus overjoyed O fruit divine
, False,,Sweet of thyself but much more sweet thus cropped
, False,,Forbidden here it seems as only fit
, False,,For Gods yet able to make Gods of Men
, False,,And why not Gods of Men since good the more
, False,,Communicated more abundant grows
, False,,The author not impaired but honored more
, False,,Here happy creature fair angelic Eve
, False,,Partake thou also happy though thou art
, False,,Happier thou mayest be worthier canst not be
, False,,Taste this and be henceforth among the Gods
, False,,Thyself a Goddess not to earth confined
, False,,But sometimes in the air as we sometimes
, False,,Ascend to Heaven by merit thine and see
, False,,What life the Gods live there and such live thou
, False,,So saying he drew nigh and to me held
, False,,Even to my mouth of that same fruit held part
, False,,Which he had plucked the pleasant savory smell
, False,,So quickened appetite that I methought
, False,,Could not but taste Forthwith up to the clouds
, False,,With him I flew and underneath beheld
, False,,The earth outstretched immense a prospect wide
, False,,And various Wondering at my flight and change
, False,,To this high exaltation suddenly
, False,,My guide was gone and I methought sunk down
, False,,And fell asleep but Oh how glad I waked
, False,,To find this but a dream Thus Eve her night
, False,,Related and thus Adam answered sad
, False,,Best image of myself and dearer half
, False,,The trouble of thy thoughts this night in sleep
, False,,Affects me equally nor can I like
, False,,This uncouth dream of evil sprung I fear
, False,,Yet evil whence in thee can harbor none
, False,,Created pure But know that in the soul
, False,,Are many lesser faculties that serve
, False,,Reason as chief among these Fancy next
, False,,Her office holds of all external things
, False,,Which the five watchful senses represent
, False,,She forms imaginations aerie shapes
, False,,Which Reason joining or disjoining frames
, False,,All what we affirm or what deny and call
, False,,Our knowledge or opinion then retires
, False,,Into her private cell when nature rests
, False,,Oft in her absence mimic Fancy wakes
, False,,To imitate her but misjoining shapes
, False,,Wild work produces oft and most in dreams
, False,,Ill matching words and deeds long past or late
, False,,Some such resemblances methinks I find
, False,,Of our last evenings talk in this thy dream
, False,,But with addition strange yet be not sad
, False,,Evil into the mind of God or man
, False,,May come and go so unreproved and leave
, False,,No spot or blame behind Which gives me hope
, False,,That what in sleep thou didst abhor to dream
, False,,Waking thou never will consent to do
, False,,Be not disheartened then nor cloud those looks
, False,,That wont to be more cheerful and serene
, False,,Than when fair morning first smiles on the world
, False,,And let us to our fresh employments rise
, False,,Among the groves the fountains and the flowers
, False,,That open now their choicest bosomed smells
, False,,Reserved from night and kept for thee in store
, False,,So cheered he his fair spouse and she was cheered
, False,,But silently a gentle tear let fall
, False,,From either eye and wiped them with her hair
, False,,Two other precious drops that ready stood
, False,,Each in their crystal sluice he ere they fell
, False,,Kissed as the gracious signs of sweet remorse
, False,,And pious awe that feared to have offended
, False,,So all was cleared and to the field they haste
, False,,But first from under shady arborous roof
, False,,Soon as they forth were come to open sight
, False,,Of dayspring and the sun who scarce uprisen

, False,,Of Paradise and Edens happy plains
, False,,Lowly they bowed adoring and began
, False,,Their orisons each morning duly paid
, False,,In various style for neither various style
, False,,Nor holy rapture wanted they to praise
, False,,Their Maker in fit strains pronounced or sung
, False,,Unmeditated such prompt eloquence
, False,,Flowed from their lips in prose or numerous verse
, False,,More tunable than needed lute or harp
, False,,To add more sweetness and they thus began
, False,,These are thy glorious works Parent of good
, False,,Almighty Thine this universal frame
, False,,Thus wondrous fair Thyself how wondrous then
, False,,Unspeakable who sits above these heavens
, False,,To us invisible or dimly seen
, False,,In these thy lowest works yet these declare
, False,,Thy goodness beyond thought and power divine
, False,,Speak ye who best can tell ye sons of light
, False,,Angels for ye behold him and with songs
, False,,And choral symphonies day without night
, False,,Circle his throne rejoicing ye in Heaven
, False,,On Earth join all ye Creatures to extol
, False,,Him first him last him midst and without end
, False,,Fairest of stars last in the train of night
, False,,If better thou belong not to the dawn
, False,,Sure pledge of day that crownest the smiling morn
, False,,With thy bright circlet praise him in thy sphere
, False,,While day arises that sweet hour of prime
, False,,Thou Sun of this great world both eye and soul
, False,,Acknowledge him thy greater sound his praise
, False,,In thy eternal course both when thou climbest
, False,,And when high noon hast gained and when thou fallest
, False,,Moon that now meetest the orient sun now flyest
, False,,With the fixed Stars fixed in their orb that flies
, False,,And ye five other wandering Fires that move
, False,,In mystic dance not without song resound
, False,,His praise who out of darkness called up light
, False,,Air and ye Elements the eldest birth
, False,,Of Natures womb that in quaternion run
, False,,Perpetual circle multiform and mix
, False,,And nourish all things let your ceaseless change
, False,,Vary to our great Maker still new praise
, False,,Ye Mists and Exhalations that now rise
, False,,From hill or steaming lake dusky or gray
, False,,Till the sun paint your fleecy skirts with gold
, False,,In honor to the worlds great Author rise
, False,,Whether to deck with clouds the uncolored sky
, False,,Or wet the thirsty earth with falling showers
, False,,Rising or falling still advance his praise
, False,,His praise ye Winds that from four quarters blow
, False,,Breathe soft or loud and wave your tops ye Pines
, False,,With every plant in sign of worship wave
, False,,Fountains and ye that warble as ye flow
, False,,Melodious murmurs warbling tune his praise
, False,,Join voices all ye living Souls Ye Birds
, False,,That singing up to Heavengate ascend
, False,,Bear on your wings and in your notes his praise
, False,,Ye that in waters glide and ye that walk
, False,,The earth and stately tread or lowly creep
, False,,Witness if I be silent morn or even

, False,,More plenty than the sun that barren shines

, False,,But in the fruitful Earth there first received
, False,,His beams unactive else their vigor find
, False,,Yet not to Earth are those bright luminaries
, False,,Officious but to thee Earths habitant
, False,,And for the Heavens wide circuit let it speak
, False,,The Makers high magnificence who built
, False,,So spacious and his line stretched out so far
, False,,That man may know he dwells not in his own
, False,,An edifice too large for him to fill
, False,,Lodged in a small partition and the rest
, False,,Ordained for uses to his Lord best known
, False,,The swiftness of those circles attribute
, False,,Though numberless to his Omnipotence
, False,,That to corporeal substances could add
, False,,Speed almost spiritual Me thou thinkest not slow
, False,,Who since the morninghour set out from Heaven
, False,,Where God resides and ere midday arrived
, False,,In Eden distance inexpressible
, False,,By numbers that have name But this I urge
, False,,Admitting motion in the Heavens to show
, False,,Invalid that which thee to doubt it moved
, False,,Not that I so affirm though so it seem
, False,,To thee who hast thy dwelling here on Earth
, False,,God to remove his ways from human sense
, False,,Placed Heaven from Earth so far that earthly sight
, False,,If it presume might err in things too high
, False,,And no advantage gain What if the sun
, False,,Be center to the world and other stars
, False,,By his attractive virtue and their own
, False,,Incited dance about him various rounds
, False,,Their wandering course now high now low then hid
, False,,Progressive retrograde or standing still
, False,,In six thou seest and what if seventh to these
, False,,The planet earth so steadfast though she seem
, False,,Insensibly three different motions move
, False,,Which else to several spheres thou must ascribe
, False,,Moved contrary with thwart obliquities
, False,,Or save the sun his labor and that swift
, False,,Nocturnal and diurnal rhomb supposed
, False,,Invisible else above all stars the wheel
, False,,Of day and night which needs not thy belief
, False,,If earth industrious of herself fetch day
, False,,Traveling east and with her part averse
, False,,From the suns beam meet night her other part
, False,,Still luminous by his ray What if that light
, False,,Sent from her through the wide transpicuous air
, False,,To the terrestrial moon be as a star
, False,,Enlightening her by day as she by night
, False,,This earth reciprocal if land be there
, False,,Fields and inhabitants Her spots thou seest
, False,,As clouds and clouds may rain and rain produce
, False,,Fruits in her softened soil for some to eat
, False,,Allotted there and other suns perhaps
, False,,With their attendant moons thou wilt descry
, False,,Communicating male and female light
, False,,Which two great sexes animate the world
, False,,Stored in each orb perhaps with some that live
, False,,For such vast room in Nature unpossessed
, False,,By living soul desert and desolate
, False,,Only to shine yet scarce to contribute
, False,,Each orb a glimpse of light conveyed so far
, False,,Down to this habitable which returns
, False,,Light back to them is obvious to dispute
, False,,But whether thus these things or whether not
, False,,But whether the sun predominant in Heaven
, False,,Rise on the earth or earth rise on the sun
, False,,He from the east his flaming road begin
, False,,Or she from west her silent course advance
, False,,With inoffensive pace that spinning sleeps
, False,,On her soft axle while she paces even
, False,,And bears thee soft with the smooth hair along
, False,,Solicit not thy thoughts with matters hid
, False,,Leave them to God above him serve and fear
, False,,Of other creatures as him pleases best
, False,,Wherever placed let him dispose joy thou
, False,,In what he gives to thee this Paradise
, False,,And thy fair Eve Heaven is for thee too high
, False,,To know what passes there be lowly wise
, False,,Think only what concerns thee and thy being
, False,,Dream not of other worlds what creatures there
, False,,Live in what state condition or degree
, False,,Contented that thus far hath been revealed
, False,,Not of Earth only but of highest Heaven
, False,,To whom thus Adam cleared of doubt replied
, False,,How fully hast thou satisfied me pure
, False,,Intelligence of Heaven angel serene
, False,,And freed from intricacies taught to live
, False,,The easiest way nor with perpleng thoughts
, False,,To interrupt the sweet of life from which
, False,,God hath bid dwell far off all anous cares
, False,,And not molest us unless we ourselves
, False,,Seek them with wandering thoughts and notions vain
, False,,But apt the mind or fancy is to rove
, False,,Unchecked and of her roving is no end
, False,,Till warned or by experience taught she learn
, False,,That not to know at large of things remote
, False,,From use obscure and subtle but to know
, False,,That which before us lies in daily life
, False,,Is the prime wisdom What is more is fume
, False,,Or emptiness or fond impertinence
, False,,And renders us in things that most concern
, False,,Unpracticed unprepared and still to seek
, False,,Therefore from this high pitch let us descend
, False,,A lower flight and speak of things at hand

, False,,Of something not unseasonable to ask

, False,,Thee I have heard relating what was done
, False,,Ere my remembrance now hear me relate
, False,,My story which perhaps thou hast not heard
, False,,And day is not yet spent till then thou seest
, False,,How subtly to detain thee I devise
, False,,Inviting thee to hear while I relate
, False,,Fond were it not in hope of thy reply
, False,,For while I sit with thee I seem in Heaven
, False,,And sweeter thy discourse is to my ear
, False,,Than fruits of palmtree pleasantest to thirst
, False,,And hunger both from labor at the hour

, False,,Imbued bring to their sweetness no satiety
, False,,To whom thus Raphael answered heavenly meek

, False,,Nor tongue ineloquent for God on thee

, False,,Inward and outward both his image fair
, False,,Speaking or mute all comeliness and grace

, False,,Nor less think we in Heaven of thee on Earth
, False,,Than of our fellowservant and inquire
, False,,Gladly into the ways of God with Man
, False,,For God we see hath honored thee and set
, False,,On man his equal love Say therefore on
, False,,For I that day was absent as befell
, False,,Bound on a voyage uncouth and obscure
, False,,Far on excursion toward the gates of Hell
, False,,Squared in full legion such command we had
, False,,To see that none thence issued forth a spy
, False,,Or enemy while God was in his work
, False,,Lest he incensed at such eruption bold

, False,,Not that they durst without his leave attempt
, False,,But us he sends upon his high behests

, False,,The dismal gates and barricaded strong

, False,,Torment and loud lament and furious rage
, False,,Glad we returned up to the coasts of light
, False,,Ere Sabbathevening so we had in charge
, False,,But thy relation now for I attend
, False,,Pleased with thy words no less than thou with mine
, False,,So spake the Godlike Power and thus our Sire
, False,,For man to tell how human life began
, False,,Is hard for who himself beginning knew
, False,,Desire with thee still longer to converse
, False,,Induced me As new waked from soundest sleep
, False,,Soft on the flowery herb I found me laid
, False,,In balmy sweat which with his beams the sun
, False,,Soon dried and on the reeking moisture fed
, False,,Straight toward Heaven my wondering eyes I turned
, False,,And gazed a while the ample sky till raised
, False,,By quick instinctive motion up I sprung
, False,,As thitherward endeavoring and upright
, False,,Stood on my feet about me round I saw
, False,,Hill dale and shady woods and sunny plains
, False,,And liquid lapse of murmuring streams by these
, False,,Creatures that lived and moved and walked or flew
, False,,Birds on the branches warbling all things smiled
, False,,With fragrance and with joy my heart oerflowed
, False,,Myself I then perused and limb by limb
, False,,Surveyed and sometimes went and sometimes ran
, False,,With supple joints as lively vigor led
, False,,But who I was or where or from what cause
, False,,Knew not to speak I tried and forthwith spake
, False,,My tongue obeyed and readily could name

, False,,And thou enlightened Earth so fresh and gay
, False,,Ye Hills and Dales ye Rivers Woods and Plains
, False,,And ye that live and move fair Creatures tell

, False,,Not of myself by some great Maker then

, False,,From whom I have that thus I move and live
, False,,And feel that I am happier than I know

, False,,From where I first drew air and first beheld
, False,,This happy light when answer none returned
, False,,On a green shady bank profuse of flowers

, False,,Insensible and forthwith to dissolve
, False,,When suddenly stood at my head a dream
, False,,Whose inward apparition gently moved
, False,,My fancy to believe I yet had being
, False,,And lived One came methought of shape divine
, False,,And said Thy mansion wants thee Adam rise
, False,,First Man of men innumerable ordained
, False,,First Father called by thee I come thy guide
, False,,To the garden of bliss thy seat prepared
, False,,So saying by the hand he took me raised
, False,,And over fields and waters as in air
, False,,Smoothsliding without step last led me up
, False,,A woody mountain whose high top was plain
, False,,A circuit wide enclosed with goodliest trees
, False,,Planted with walks and bowers that what I saw
, False,,Of Earth before scarce pleasant seemed Each tree
, False,,Loaden with fairest fruit that hung to the eye
, False,,Tempting stirred in me sudden appetite
, False,,To pluck and eat whereat I waked and found
, False,,Before mine eyes all real as the dream
, False,,Had lively shadowed Here had new begun
, False,,My wandering had not he who was my guide
, False,,Up hither from among the trees appeared
, False,,Presence Divine Rejoicing but with awe
, False,,In adoration at his feet I fell
, False,,Submiss He reared me and Whom thou soughtest I am
, False,,Said mildly Author of all this thou seest
, False,,Above or round about thee or beneath
, False,,This Paradise I give thee count it thine
, False,,To till and keep and of the fruit to eat
, False,,Of every tree that in the garden grows
, False,,Eat freely with glad heart fear here no dearth
, False,,But of the tree whose operation brings
, False,,Knowledge of good and ill which I have set

, False,,And shun the bitter consequence for know

, False,,Transgressed inevitably thou shalt die
, False,,From that day mortal and this happy state
, False,,Shalt lose expelled from hence into a world

, False,,The rigid interdiction which resounds
, False,,Yet dreadful in mine ear though in my choice

, False,,Returned and gracious purpose thus renewed
, False,,Not only these fair bounds but all the Earth
, False,,To thee and to thy race I give as lords
, False,,Possess it and all things that therein live
, False,,Or live in sea or air beast fish and fowl

, False,,From thee their names and pay thee fealty
, False,,With low subjection understand the same

, False,,Not hither summoned since they cannot change

, False,,Approaching two and two these cowering low
, False,,With blandishment each bird stooped on his wing
, False,,I named them as they passed and understood

, False,,My sudden apprehension But in these
, False,,I found not what methought I wanted still
, False,,And to the heavenly Vision thus presumed
, False,,Oh by what name for thou above all these
, False,,Above mankind or aught than mankind higher
, False,,Surpassest far my naming how may I
, False,,Adore thee Author of this universe
, False,,And all this good to man for whose well being
, False,,So amply and with hands so liberal
, False,,Thou hast provided all things But with me
, False,,I see not who partakes In solitude
, False,,What happiness who can enjoy alone
, False,,Or all enjoying what contentment find
, False,,Thus I presumptuous and the Vision bright
, False,,As with a smile more brightened thus replied
, False,,What callest thou solitude Is not the Earth
, False,,With various living creatures and the air
, False,,Replenished and all these at thy command
, False,,To come and play before thee Knowest thou not
, False,,Their language and their ways They also know
, False,,And reason not contemptibly With these
, False,,Find pastime and bear rule thy realm is large
, False,,So spake the Universal Lord and seemed
, False,,So ordering I with leave of speech implored
, False,,And humble deprecation thus replied
, False,,Let not my words offend thee Heavenly Power
, False,,My Maker be propitious while I speak
, False,,Hast thou not made me here thy substitute
, False,,And these inferior far beneath me set
, False,,Among unequals what society
, False,,Can sort what harmony or true delight
, False,,Which must be mutual in proportion due
, False,,Given and received but in disparity
, False,,The one intense the other still remiss
, False,,Cannot well suit with either but soon prove
, False,,Tedious alike Of fellowship I speak
, False,,Such as I seek fit to participate
, False,,All rational delight wherein the brute
, False,,Cannot be human consort They rejoice
, False,,Each with their kind lion with lioness
, False,,So fitly them in pairs thou hast combined
, False,,Much less can bird with beast or fish with fowl
, False,,So well converse nor with the ox the ape
, False,,Worse then can man with beast and least of all
, False,,Whereto the Almighty answered not displeased
, False,,A nice and subtle happiness I see

, False,,Of thy associates Adam and wilt taste
, False,,No pleasure though in pleasure solitary
, False,,What thinkest thou then of me and this my state
, False,,Seem I to thee sufficiently possessed
, False,,Of happiness or not who am alone
, False,,From all eternity for none I know
, False,,Second to me or like equal much less
, False,,How have I then with whom to hold converse
, False,,Save with the creatures which I made and those
, False,,To me inferior infinite descents
, False,,Beneath what other creatures are to thee
, False,,He ceased I lowly answered To attain
, False,,The heighth and depth of thy eternal ways
, False,,All human thoughts come short Supreme of things
, False,,Thou in thyself art perfect and in thee
, False,,Is no deficience found Not so is Man
, False,,But in degree the cause of his desire
, False,,By conversation with his like to help
, False,,Or solace his defects No need that thou
, False,,Shouldst propagate already Infinite
, False,,And through all numbers absolute though One
, False,,But man by number is to manifest
, False,,His single imperfection and beget
, False,,Like of his like his image multiplied
, False,,In unity defective which requires
, False,,Collateral love and dearest amity
, False,,Thou in thy secrecy although alone

, False,,Of union or communion deified

, False,,Permissive and acceptance found which gained

, False,,Impresses quaint caparisons and steeds
, False,,Bases and tinsel trappings gorgeous knights
, False,,At joust and tournament then marshaled feast
, False,,Served up in hall with sewers and seneschals
, False,,The skill of artifice or office mean
, False,,Not that which justly gives heroic name
, False,,To person or to poem Me of these
, False,,Nor skilled nor studious higher argument
, False,,Remains sufficient of itself to raise
, False,,That name unless an age too late or cold
, False,,Climate or years damp my intended wing
, False,,Depressed and much they may if all be mine
, False,,Not hers who brings it nightly to my ear
, False,,The sun was sunk and after him the star
, False,,Of Hesperus whose office is to bring
, False,,Twilight upon the earth short arbiter
, False,,Twixt day and night and now from end to end

, False,,When Satan who late fled before the threats
, False,,Of Gabriel out of Eden now improved
, False,,In meditated fraud and malice bent
, False,,On Mans destruction maugre what might hap
, False,,Of heavier on himself fearless returned
, False,,By night he fled and at midnight returned
, False,,From compassing the earth cautious of day
, False,,Since Uriel regent of the sun descried
, False,,His entrance and forewarned the Cherubim
, False,,That kept their watch thence full of anguish driven
, False,,The space of seven continued nights he rode
, False,,With darkness thrice the equinoctial line
, False,,He circled four times crossed the car of night
, False,,From pole to pole traversing each colure
, False,,On the eighth returned and on the coast averse
, False,,From entrance or Cherubic watch by stealth
, False,,Found unsuspected way There was a place
, False,,Now not though sin not time first wrought the change
, False,,Where Tigris at the foot of Paradise
, False,,Into a gulf shot under ground till part

, False,,In with the river sunk and with it rose

, False,,Where to lie hid sea he had searched and land

, False,,With narrow search and with inspection deep
, False,,Considered every creature which of all
, False,,Most opportune might serve his wiles and found
, False,,The Serpent subtlest beast of all the field
, False,,Him after long debate irresolute
, False,,Of thoughts revolved his final sentence chose
, False,,Fit vessel fittest imp of fraud in whom
, False,,To enter and his dark suggestions hide
, False,,From sharpest sight for in the wily snake
, False,,Whatever sleights none would suspicious mark
, False,,As from his wit and native subtlety
, False,,Proceeding which in other beasts observed
, False,,Doubt might beget of diabolic power
, False,,Active within beyond the sense of brute

, False,,His bursting passion into plaints thus poured

, False,,With second thoughts reforming what was old
, False,,Oh Earth how like to Heaven if not preferred
, False,,For what God after better worse would build
, False,,Terrestrial Heaven danced round by other Heavens
, False,,That shine yet bear their bright officious lamps
, False,,Light above light for thee alone as seems
, False,,In thee concentering all their precious beams
, False,,Of sacred influence As God in Heaven
, False,,Is center yet extends to all so thou
, False,,Centering receivest from all those orbs in thee
, False,,Not in themselves all their known virtue appears
, False,,Productive in herb plant and nobler birth
, False,,Of creatures animate with gradual life
, False,,Of growth sense reason all summed up in Man

, False,,If I could joy in aught sweet interchange
, False,,Of hill and valley rivers woods and plains
, False,,Now land now sea and shores with forest crowned
, False,,Rocks dens and caves But I in none of these
, False,,Find place or refuge and the more I see
, False,,Pleasures about me so much more I feel
, False,,Torment within me as from the hateful siege
, False,,Of contraries all good to me becomes
, False,,Bane and in Heaven much worse would be my state
