, False,,As I though thereby worse to me redound
, False,,For only in destroying I find ease
, False,,To my relentless thoughts and him destroyed
, False,,Or won to what may work his utter loss
, False,,For whom all this was made all this will soon
, False,,Follow as to him linked in weal or woe
, False,,In woe then that destruction wide may range
, False,,To me shall be the glory sole among
, False,,The infernal Powers in one day to have marred
, False,,What he Almighty styled six nights and days
, False,,Continued making and who knows how long
, False,,Before had been contriving though perhaps
, False,,Not longer than since I in one night freed
, False,,From servitude inglorious well nigh half
, False,,The angelic name and thinner left the throng
, False,,Of his adorers He to be avenged
, False,,And to repair his numbers thus impaired
, False,,Whether such virtue spent of old now failed
, False,,More angels to create if they at least
, False,,Are his created or to spite us more
, False,,Determined to advance into our room
, False,,A creature formed of earth and him endow
, False,,Exalted from so base original
, False,,With heavenly spoils our spoils What he decreed
, False,,He effected man he made and for him built
, False,,Magnificent this world and earth his seat

, False,,That to the heighth of Deity aspired

, False,,Descend to Who aspires must down as low

, False,,To basest things Revenge at first though sweet
, False,,Bitter ere long back on itself recoils

, False,,Provokes my envy this new favorite
, False,,Of Heaven this man of clay son of despite
, False,,Whom us the more to spite his Maker raised
, False,,From dust Spite then with spite is best repaid
, False,,So saying through each thicket dank or dry

, False,,The serpent him fastsleeping soon he found
, False,,In labyrinth of many a round selfrolled
, False,,His head the midst well stored with subtle wiles
, False,,Not yet in horrid shade or dismal den
, False,,Nor nocent yet but on the grassy herb
, False,,Fearless unfeared he slept in at his mouth
, False,,The devil entered and his brutal sense
, False,,In heart or head possessing soon inspired
, False,,With act intelligential but his sleep
, False,,Disturbed not waiting close the approach of morn
, False,,Now when as sacred light began to dawn
, False,,In Eden on the humid flowers that breathed

, False,,With grateful smell forth came the human pair

, False,,The hands dispatch of two gardening so wide

, False,,This garden still to tend plant herb and flower
, False,,Our pleasant task enjoined but till more hands
, False,,Aid us the work under our labor grows
, False,,Luxurious by restraint what we by day
, False,,Lop overgrown or prune or prop or bind

, False,,Tending to wild Thou therefore now advise
, False,,Or bear what to my mind first thoughts present
, False,,Let us divide our labors thou where choice
, False,,Leads thee or where most needs whether to wind

, False,,The clasping ivy where to climb while I

, False,,For while so near each other thus all day
, False,,Our task we choose what wonder if so near
, False,,Looks intervene and smiles or object new
, False,,Casual discourse draw on which intermits
, False,,Our days work brought to little though begun
, False,,Early and the hour of supper comes unearned
, False,,To whom mild answer Adam thus returned
, False,,Sole Eve associate sole to me beyond
, False,,Compare above all living creatures dear
, False,,Well hast thou motioned well thy thoughts employed
, False,,How we might best fulfill the work which here
, False,,God hath assigned us nor of me shalt pass
, False,,Unpraised for nothing lovelier can be found
, False,,In woman than to study household good
, False,,And good works in her husband to promote

, False,,Labor as to debar us when we need
, False,,Refreshment whether food or talk between
, False,,Food of the mind or this sweet intercourse
, False,,Of looks and smiles for smiles from reason flow
, False,,To brute denied and are of love the food
, False,,Love not the lowest end of human life
, False,,For not to irksome toil but to delight
, False,,He made us and delight to reason joined
, False,,These paths and bowers doubt not but our joint hands
, False,,Will keep from wilderness with ease as wide
, False,,As we need walk till younger hands ere long
, False,,Assist us But if much converse perhaps
, False,,Thee satiate to short absence I could yield
, False,,For solitude sometimes is best society
, False,,And short retirement urges sweet return
, False,,But other doubt possesses me lest harm
, False,,Befall thee severed from me for thou knowest
, False,,What hath been warned us what malicious foe
, False,,Envying our happiness and of his own
, False,,Despairing seeks to work us woe and shame
, False,,By sly assault and somewhere nigh at hand
, False,,Watches no doubt with greedy hope to find
, False,,His wish and best advantage us asunder
, False,,Hopeless to circumvent us joined where each
, False,,To other speedy aid might lend at need

, False,,Our fealty from God or to disturb
, False,,Conjugal love than which perhaps no bliss
, False,,Enjoyed by us excites his envy more
, False,,Or this or worse leave not the faithful side
, False,,That gave thee being still shades thee and protects
, False,,The wife where danger or dishonor lurks
, False,,Safest and seemliest by her husband stays
, False,,Who guards her or with her the worst endures
, False,,To whom the virgin majesty of Eve
, False,,As one who loves and some unkindness meets
, False,,With sweet austere composure thus replied
, False,,Offspring of Heaven and Earth and all Earths Lord
, False,,That such an enemy we have who seeks
, False,,Our ruin both by thee informed I learn
, False,,And from the parting angel overheard
, False,,As in a shady nook I stood behind
, False,,Just then returned at shut of evening flowers

, False,,To God or thee because we have a foe
, False,,May tempt it I expected not to hear
, False,,His violence thou fearest not being such
, False,,As we not capable of death or pain
, False,,Can either not receive or can repel
, False,,His fraud is then thy fear which plain infers
, False,,Thy equal fear that my firm faith and love
, False,,Can by his fraud be shaken or seduced

, False,,Adam misthought of her to thee so dear
, False,,To whom with healing words Adam replied
, False,,Daughter of God and Man immortal Eve
, False,,For such thou art from sin and blame entire
, False,,Not diffident of thee do I dissuade
, False,,Thy absence from my sight but to avoid
, False,,The attempt itself intended by our foe
, False,,For he who tempts though in vain at least asperses
, False,,The tempted with dishonor foul supposed
, False,,Not incorruptible of faith not proof
, False,,Against temptation Thou thyself with scorn
, False,,And anger wouldst resent the offered wrong
, False,,Though ineffectual found misdeem not then
, False,,If such affront I labor to avert
, False,,From thee alone which on us both at once
, False,,The enemy though bold will hardly dare
, False,,Or daring first on me the assault shall light
, False,,Nor thou his malice and false guile contemn
, False,,Subtle he needs must be who could seduce
, False,,Angels nor think superfluous others aid
, False,,I from the influence of thy looks receive
, False,,Access in every virtue in thy sight
, False,,More wise more watchful stronger if need were
, False,,Of outward strength while shame thou looking on
, False,,Shame to be overcome or overreached
, False,,Would utmost vigor raise and raised unite
, False,,Why shouldst not thou like sense within thee feel
, False,,When I am present and thy trial choose
, False,,With me best witness of thy virtue tried
, False,,So spake domestic Adam in his care
, False,,And matrimonial love but Eve who thought
, False,,Less attributed to her faith sincere
, False,,Thus her reply with accent sweet renewed
, False,,If this be our condition thus to dwell
, False,,In narrow circuit straitened by a foe
, False,,Subtle or violent we not endued
, False,,Single with like defense wherever met
, False,,How are we happy still in fear of harm
, False,,But harm precedes not sin only our foe
, False,,Tempting affronts us with his foul esteem
, False,,Of our integrity his foul esteem
, False,,Sticks no dishonor on our front but turns
, False,,Foul on himself then wherefore shunned or feared
, False,,By us who rather double honor gain
, False,,From his surmise proved false find peace within
, False,,Favor from Heaven our witness from the event
, False,,And what is faith love virtue unassayed
, False,,Alone without exterior help sustained
, False,,Let us not then suspect our happy state
, False,,Left so imperfect by the Maker wise
, False,,As not secure to single or combined
, False,,Frail is our happiness if this be so
, False,,And Eden were no Eden thus exposed
, False,,To whom thus Adam fervently replied
, False,,Oh Woman best are all things as the will
, False,,Of God ordained them His creating hand
, False,,Nothing imperfect or deficient left
, False,,Of all that he created much less Man

, False,,Secure from outward force within himself

, False,,Against his will he can receive no harm

, False,,Reason is free and Reason he made right
, False,,But bid her well be ware and still erect

, False,,Wouldst thou approve thy constancy approve
, False,,First thy obedience the other who can know
, False,,Not seeing thee attempted who attest
, False,,But if thou think trial unsought may find
, False,,Us both securer than thus warned thou seemest

, False,,For God towards thee hath done his part do thine

, False,,Of thy presumed return event perverse
, False,,Thou never from that hour in Paradise
, False,,Foundst either sweet repast or sound repose

, False,,From her best prop so far and storm so nigh

, False,,Or of revived Adonis or renowned
, False,,Alcinous host of old Laertes son

, False,,Such pleasure took the Serpent to behold
, False,,This flowery plat the sweet recess of Eve
, False,,Thus early thus alone Her heavenly form
, False,,Angelic but more soft and feminine

, False,,Of gesture or least action overawed

, False,,The woman opportune to all attempts

, False,,Whose higher intellectual more I shun

, False,,So spake the enemy of mankind enclosed

, False,,His fraudulent temptation thus began

, False,,By angels numberless thy daily train

, False,,What may this mean language of man pronounced
, False,,By tongue of brute and human sense expressed
, False,,The first at least of these I thought denied
, False,,To beasts whom God on their creationday

, False,,Much reason and in their actions oft appears

, False,,I knew but not with human voice endued

, False,,How camest thou speakable of mute and how
, False,,To me so friendly grown above the rest

, False,,To whom the guileful Tempter thus replied

, False,,Easy to me it is to tell thee all
, False,,What thou commandest and right thou shouldst be obeyed

, False,,The trodden herb of abject thoughts and low

, False,,Or sex and apprehended nothing high

, False,,Ruddy and gold I nearer drew to gaze

, False,,At feed or fountain never had I found
, False,,Sated at length ere long I might perceive

, False,,Wanted not long though to this shape retained

, False,,But say where grows the tree from hence how far
, False,,For many are the trees of God that grow
, False,,In Paradise and various yet unknown
, False,,To us in such abundance lies our choice
, False,,As leaves a greater store of fruit untouched
, False,,Still hanging incorruptible till men
, False,,Grow up to their provision and more hands
, False,,Help to disburden Nature of her birth
, False,,To whom the wily adder blithe and glad

, False,,My conduct I can bring thee thither soon
, False,,Lead then said Eve He leading swiftly rolled
, False,,In tangles and made intricate seem straight

, False,,Compact of unctuous vapor which the night
, False,,Condenses and the cold environs round
, False,,Kindled through agitation to a flame

, False,,The Tempter but with show of zeal and love

, False,,New part puts on and as to passion moved

, False,,Warmed by the sun producing every kind

, False,,Pausing a while thus to herself she mused

, False,,Though kept from man and worthy to be admired
, False,,Whose taste too long forborne at first assay
, False,,Gave elocution to the mute and taught
, False,,The tongue not made for speech to speak thy praise
, False,,Thy praise he also who forbids thy use

, False,,For good unknown sure is not had or had

, False,,In plain then what forbids he but to know
, False,,Forbids us good forbids us to be wise
, False,,Such prohibitions bind not But if death
, False,,Bind us with afterbands what profits then
, False,,Our inward freedom In the day we eat

, False,,For beasts it seems yet that one beast which first
, False,,Hath tasted envies not but brings with joy

, False,,To reach and feed at once both body and mind

, False,,Thus to herself she pleasingly began

, False,,In Paradise of operation blest
, False,,To sapience hitherto obscured infamed

, False,,Not without song each morning and due praise

, False,,Best guide not following thee I had remained

, False,,And givest access though secret she retire

, False,,This may be well But what if God have seen

, False,,And me with thee hath ruined for with thee

, False,,How can I live without thee how forego
, False,,Thy sweet converse and love so dearly joined

, False,,Had it been only coveting to eye

, False,,From Earth arrived at Heavengate displeased
, False,,All were who heard dim sadness did not spare
, False,,That time celestial visages yet mixed
, False,,With pity violated not their bliss
, False,,About the newarrived in multitudes
, False,,The ethereal people ran to hear and know
, False,,How all befell They towards the throne supreme
, False,,Accountable made haste to make appear
, False,,With righteous plea their utmost vigilance
, False,,And easily approved when the Most High
, False,,Eternal Father from his secret cloud
, False,,Amidst in thunder uttered thus his voice
, False,,Assembled angels and ye Powers returned
, False,,From unsuccessful charge be not dismayed
, False,,Nor troubled at these tidings from the earth
, False,,Which your sincerest care could not prevent
, False,,Foretold so lately what would come to pass
, False,,When first this tempter crossed the gulf from Hell
, False,,I told ye then he should prevail and speed
, False,,On his bad errand man should be seduced
, False,,And flattered out of all believing lies
, False,,Against his Maker no decree of mine

, False,,Or touch with lightest moment of impulse
, False,,His free will to her own inclining left
, False,,In even scale But fallen he is and now
, False,,What rests but that the mortal sentence pass
, False,,On his transgression death denounced that day
, False,,Which he presumes already vain and void
, False,,Because not yet inflicted as he feared
, False,,By some immediate stroke but soon shall find
, False,,Forbearance no acquittance ere day end
, False,,Justice shall not return as bounty scorned
, False,,But whom send I to judge them whom but thee
, False,,Vicegerent Son To thee I have transferred
, False,,All judgment whether in Heaven or Earth or Hell
, False,,Easy it may be seen that I intend
, False,,Mercy colleague with justice sending thee
, False,,Mans friend his Mediator his designed
, False,,Both ransom and Redeemer voluntary
, False,,And destined man himself to judge man fallen
, False,,So spake the Father and unfolding bright

, False,,Approaching thus to Adam called aloud

, False,,Absents thee or what chance detains Come forth

, False,,And gavest me as thy perfect gift so good

, False,,To whom the Sovereign Presence thus replied

, False,,Before his voice or was she made thy guide

, False,,Above all cattle each beast of the field

, False,,Cursed is the ground for thy sake thou in sorrow

, False,,Thorns also and thistles it shall bring thee forth
, False,,Unbid and thou shalt eat the herb of the field
, False,,In the sweat of thy face shalt thou eat bread

, False,,For dust thou art and shalt to dust return

, False,,Smooth easy inoffensive down to Hell

, False,,From Susa his Memnonian palace high

, False,,What I have done what suffered with what pain
, False,,Voyaged the unreal vast unbounded deep

, False,,Their appetite with gust instead of fruit

, False,,Into the same illusion not as man
, False,,Whom they triumphed once lapsed Thus were they plagued
, False,,And worn with famine long and ceaseless hiss

, False,,Among the Heathen of their purchase got

, False,,This said they both betook them several ways

, False,,To Adam what shall come in future days
, False,,As I shall thee enlighten intermix
, False,,My covenant in the Womans seed renewed
, False,,So send them forth though sorrowing yet in peace
, False,,And on the east side of the garden place
, False,,Where entrance up from Eden easiest climbs
, False,,Cherubic watch and of a sword the flame
, False,,Widewaving all approach far off to fright
, False,,And guard all passage to the tree of life
, False,,Lest Paradise a receptacle prove
, False,,To Spirits foul and all my trees their prey
, False,,With whose stolen fruit man once more to delude
, False,,He ceased and the archangelic power prepared
, False,,For swift descent with him the cohort bright
, False,,Of watchful Cherubim four faces each
, False,,Had like a double Janus all their shape
, False,,Spangled with eyes more numerous than those
, False,,Of Argus and more wakeful than to drowse
, False,,Charmed with Arcadian pipe the pastoral reed
, False,,Of Hermes or his opiate rod Mean while
, False,,To resalute the world with sacred light
, False,,Leucothea waked and with fresh dews imbalmed
, False,,The earth when Adam and first matron Eve
, False,,Had ended now their orisons and found
, False,,Strength added from above new hope to spring
, False,,Out of despair joy but with fear yet linked
, False,,Which thus to Eve his welcome words renewed
, False,,Eve easily may faith admit that all
, False,,The good which we enjoy from Heaven descends
, False,,But that from us aught should ascend to Heaven
, False,,So prevalent as to concern the mind
, False,,Of God highblest or to incline his will
, False,,Hard to belief may seem yet this will prayer
, False,,Or one short sigh of human breath upborne
, False,,Even to the seat of God For since I sought
, False,,By prayer the offended Deity to appease
, False,,Kneeled and before him humbled all my heart
, False,,Methought I saw him placable and mild
, False,,Bending his ear persuasion in me grew
, False,,That I was heard with favor peace returned
, False,,Home to my breast and to my memory
, False,,His promise that thy seed shall bruise our foe
, False,,Which then not minded in dismay yet now
, False,,Assures me that the bitterness of death
, False,,Is past and we shall live Whence hail to thee
, False,,Eve rightly called mother of all mankind
, False,,Mother of all things living since by thee
, False,,Man is to live and all things live for Man
, False,,To whom thus Eve with sad demeanor meek
, False,,Illworthy I such title should belong
, False,,To me transgressor who for thee ordained
, False,,A help became thy snare to me reproach
, False,,Rather belongs distrust and all dispraise
, False,,But infinite in pardon was my Judge
, False,,That I who first brought death on all am graced
, False,,The source of life next favorable thou
, False,,Who highly thus to entitle me vouchsafst
, False,,Far other name deserving But the field
, False,,To labor calls us now with sweat imposed
, False,,Though after sleepless night for see the morn
, False,,All unconcerned with our unrest begins
, False,,Her rosy progress smiling let us forth
, False,,I never from thy side henceforth to stray
, False,,Whereer our days work lies though now enjoined
, False,,Laborious till day droop while here we dwell
, False,,What can be toilsome in these pleasant walks
, False,,Here let us live though in fallen state content
, False,,So spake so wished much humbled Eve but fate
, False,,Subscribed not nature first gave signs impressed
, False,,On bird beast air air suddenly eclipsed
, False,,After short blush of morn nigh in her sight
, False,,The bird of Jove stooped from his aerie tour
, False,,Two birds of gayest plume before him drove
, False,,Down from a hill the beast that reigns in woods
, False,,First hunter then pursued a gentle brace
, False,,Goodliest of all the forest hart and hind
, False,,Direct to the eastern gate was bent their flight
, False,,Adam observed and with his eye the chase
, False,,Pursuing not unmoved to Eve thus spake
, False,,Oh Eve some further change awaits us nigh
, False,,Which Heaven by these mute signs in Nature shows
, False,,Forerunners of his purpose or to warn
, False,,Us haply too secure of our discharge
, False,,From penalty because from death released
, False,,Some days how long and what till then our life
, False,,Who knows or more than this that we are dust
, False,,And thither must return and be no more
, False,,Why else this double object in our sight
, False,,Of flight pursued in the air and oer the ground
, False,,One way the selfsame hour why in the east
, False,,Darkness ere days midcourse and morninglight
, False,,More orient in yon western cloud that draws
, False,,Oer the blue firmament a radiant white
, False,,And slow descends with something heavenly fraught
, False,,He erred not for by this the heavenly bands
, False,,Down from a sky of jasper lighted now
, False,,In Paradise and on a hill made halt
, False,,A glorious apparition had not doubt
, False,,And carnal fear that day dimmed Adams eye
, False,,Not that more glorious when the angels met
, False,,Jacob in Mahanaim where he saw
, False,,The field pavilioned with his guardians bright
, False,,Nor that which on the flaming mount appeared
, False,,In Dothan covered with a camp of fire
, False,,Against the Syrian king who to surprise
, False,,One man assassinlike had levied war
, False,,War unproclaimed The princely hierarch
, False,,In their bright stand there left his powers to seize
, False,,Possession of the garden he alone
, False,,To find where Adam sheltered took his way
, False,,Not unperceived of Adam who to Eve
, False,,While the great visitant approached thus spake
, False,,Eve now expect great tidings which perhaps
, False,,Of us will soon determine or impose
, False,,New laws to be observed for I descry
, False,,From yonder blazing cloud that veils the hill
, False,,One of the heavenly host and by his gait
, False,,None of the meanest some great potentate
, False,,Or of the Thrones above such majesty
, False,,Invests him coming yet not terrible
, False,,That I should fear nor sociably mild
, False,,As Raphael that I should much confide
, False,,But solemn and sublime whom not to offend
, False,,With reverence I must meet and thou retire
, False,,He ended and the archangel soon drew nigh
, False,,Not in his shape celestial but as man
, False,,Clad to meet man over his lucid arms
, False,,A military vest of purple flowed
, False,,Livelier than Meliboean or the grain
, False,,Of Sarra worn by kings and heroes old
, False,,In time of truce Iris had dipped the woof
, False,,His starry helm unbuckled showed him prime
, False,,In manhood where youth ended by his side
, False,,As in a glistering zodiac hung the sword
, False,,Satans dire dread and in his hand the spear
, False,,Adam bowed low he kingly from his state
, False,,Inclined not but his coming thus declared
, False,,Adam Heavens high behest no preface needs
, False,,Sufficient that thy prayers are heard and Death
, False,,Then due by sentence when thou didst transgress
, False,,Defeated of his seizure many days
, False,,Given thee of grace wherein thou mayest repent
, False,,And one bad act with many deeds well done
, False,,Mayest cover Well may then thy Lord appeased
, False,,Redeem thee quite from Deaths rapacious claim
, False,,But longer in this Paradise to dwell
, False,,Permits not to remove thee I am come
, False,,And send thee from the garden forth to till
, False,,The ground whence thou wast taken fitter soil
, False,,He added not for Adam at the news
, False,,Heartstruck with chilling gripe of sorrow stood
, False,,That all his senses bound Eve who unseen
, False,,Yet all had heard with audible lament
, False,,Discovered soon the place of her retire
, False,,Oh unexpected stroke worse than of death
, False,,Must I thus leave thee Paradise thus leave
, False,,Thee native soil these happy walks and shades
, False,,Fit haunt of Gods where I had hope to spend
, False,,Quiet though sad the respite of that day
, False,,That must be mortal to us both Oh flowers
, False,,That never will in other climate grow
, False,,My early visitation and my last
, False,,At even which I bred up with tender hand
, False,,From the first opening bud and gave ye names
, False,,Who now shall rear ye to the sun or rank
, False,,Your tribes and water from the ambrosial fount
, False,,Thee lastly nuptial bower by me adorned
, False,,With what to sight or smell was sweet from thee
, False,,How shall I part and whither wander down
, False,,Into a lower world to this obscure
, False,,And wild how shall we breathe in other air
, False,,Less pure accustomed to immortal fruits
, False,,Whom thus the angel interrupted mild
, False,,Lament not Eve but patiently resign
, False,,What justly thou hast lost nor set thy heart
, False,,Thus overfond on that which is not thine
, False,,Thy going is not lonely with thee goes
, False,,Thy husband whom to follow thou art bound
, False,,Where he abides think there thy native soil
, False,,Adam by this from the cold sudden damp
, False,,Recovering and his scattered spirits returned
, False,,To Michael thus his humble words addressed
, False,,Celestial whether among the Thrones or named
, False,,Of them the highest for such of shape may seem
, False,,Prince above princes gently hast thou told
, False,,Thy message which might else in telling wound
, False,,And in performing end us what besides
, False,,Of sorrow and dejection and despair
, False,,Our frailty can sustain thy tidings bring
, False,,Departure from this happy place our sweet
, False,,Recess and only consolation left
, False,,Familiar to our eyes all places else
, False,,Inhospitable appear and desolate
, False,,Nor knowing us nor known And if by prayer
, False,,Incessant I could hope to change the will
, False,,Of Him who all things can I would not cease
, False,,To weary him with my assiduous cries
, False,,But prayer against his absolute decree
, False,,No more avails than breath against the wind
, False,,Blown stifling back on him that breathes it forth
, False,,Therefore to his great bidding I submit
, False,,This most afflicts me that departing hence
, False,,As from his face I shall be hid deprived
, False,,His blessed countenance Here I could frequent
, False,,With worship place by place where he vouchsafed
, False,,Presence Divine and to my sons relate
, False,,On this mount he appeared under this tree
, False,,Stood visible among these pines his voice
, False,,I heard here with him at this fountain talked
, False,,So many grateful altars I would rear
, False,,Of grassy turf and pile up every stone
, False,,Of luster from the brook in memory
, False,,Or monument to ages and thereon
, False,,Offer sweetsmelling gums and fruits and flowers
, False,,In yonder nether world where shall I seek
, False,,His bright appearances or footstep trace
, False,,For though I fled him angry yet recalled
, False,,To life prolonged and promised race I now
, False,,Gladly behold though but his utmost skirts
, False,,Of glory and far off his steps adore
, False,,To whom thus Michael with regard benign
, False,,Adam thou knowest Heaven his and all the Earth
, False,,Not this rock only his Omnipresence fills
, False,,Land sea and air and every kind that lives
, False,,Fomented by his virtual power and warmed
, False,,All the earth he gave thee to possess and rule
, False,,No despicable gift surmise not then
, False,,His presence to these narrow bounds confined
, False,,Of Paradise or Eden this had been
, False,,Perhaps thy capital seat from whence had spread
, False,,All generations and had hither come
, False,,From all the ends of the earth to celebrate
, False,,And reverence thee their great progenitor
, False,,But this preeminence thou hast lost brought down
, False,,To dwell on even ground now with thy sons
, False,,Yet doubt not but in valley and in plain
, False,,God is as here and will be found alike
, False,,Present and of his presence many a sign
, False,,Still following thee still compassing thee round
, False,,With goodness and paternal love his face
, False,,Express and of his steps the track divine
, False,,Which that thou mayest believe and be confirmed
, False,,Ere thou from hence depart know I am sent
, False,,To show thee what shall come in future days
, False,,To thee and to thy offspring good with bad
, False,,Expect to hear supernal grace contending
, False,,With sinfulness of men thereby to learn
, False,,True patience and to temper joy with fear
, False,,And pious sorrow equally inured
, False,,By moderation either state to bear
, False,,Prosperous or adverse so shalt thou lead
, False,,Safest thy life and best prepared endure
, False,,Thy mortal passage when it comes Ascend
, False,,This hill let Eve for I have drenched her eyes
, False,,Here sleep below while thou to foresight wakest
, False,,As once thou sleptst while she to life was formed
, False,,To whom thus Adam gratefully replied
, False,,Ascend I follow thee safe Guide the path
, False,,Thou leadest me and to the hand of Heaven submit
, False,,However chastening to the evil turn
, False,,My obvious breast arming to overcome
, False,,By suffering and earn rest from labor won
, False,,If so I may attain So both ascend
, False,,In the visions of God It was a hill
, False,,Of Paradise the highest from whose top
, False,,The hemisphere of earth in clearest ken
, False,,Stretched out to the amplest reach of prospect lay
, False,,Not higher that hill nor wider looking round
, False,,Whereon for different cause the Tempter set
, False,,Our second Adam in the wilderness
, False,,To show him all Earths kingdoms and their glory
, False,,His eye might there command wherever stood
, False,,City of old or modern fame the seat
, False,,Of mightiest empire from the destined walls
, False,,Of Cambalu seat of Cathaian Can
, False,,And Samarchand by Oxus Temirs throne
, False,,To Paquin of Sinaean kings and thence
, False,,To Agra and Lahor of great Mogul
, False,,Down to the golden Chersonese or where
, False,,The Persian in Ecbatan sat or since
, False,,In Hispahan or where the Russian Czar
, False,,In Moscow or the Sultan in Bizance
, False,,Turkestanborn nor could his eye not ken
, False,,The empire of Negus to his utmost port
, False,,Ercoco and the less maritime kings
, False,,Mombaza and Quiloa and Melind
, False,,And Sofala thought Ophir to the realm
, False,,Of Congo and Angola farthest south
, False,,Or thence from Niger flood to Atlas mount
, False,,The kingdoms of Almansor Fez and Sus
, False,,Morocco and Algiers and Tremisen
, False,,On Europe thence and where Rome was to sway
, False,,The world in spirit perhaps he also saw
, False,,Rich Meco the seat of Montezuma
, False,,And Cusco in Peru the richer seat
, False,,Of Atabalipa and yet unspoiled
, False,,Guiana whose great city Geryons sons
, False,,Call El Dorado But to nobler sights
, False,,Michael from Adams eyes the film removed
, False,,Which that false fruit that promised clearer sight
, False,,Had bred then purged with euphrasy and rue
, False,,The visual nerve for he had much to see
, False,,And from the well of life three drops instilled
, False,,So deep the power of these ingredients pierced
, False,,Even to the inmost seat of mental sight
, False,,That Adam now enforced to close his eyes
, False,,Sunk down and all his spirits became entranced
, False,,But him the gentle angel by the hand
, False,,Soon raised and his attention thus recalled
, False,,Adam now open thine eyes and first behold
, False,,The effects which thy original crime hath wrought
, False,,In some to spring from thee who never touched
, False,,The excepted tree nor with the snake conspired
, False,,Nor sinned thy sin yet from that sin derive
, False,,Corruption to bring forth more violent deeds
, False,,His eyes he opened and beheld a field
, False,,Part arable and tilth whereon were sheaves
, False,,New reaped the other part sheepwalks and folds
, False,,I the midst an altar as the landmark stood
, False,,Rustic of grassy sord thither anon
, False,,A sweaty reaper from his tillage brought
, False,,First fruits the green ear and the yellow sheaf
, False,,Unculled as came to hand a shepherd next
, False,,More meek came with the firstlings of his flock
, False,,Choicest and best then sacrificing laid
, False,,The inwards and their fat with incense strowed
, False,,On the cleft wood and all due rights performed
, False,,His offering soon propitious fire from Heaven
, False,,Consumed with nimble glance and grateful steam
, False,,The others not for his was not sincere
, False,,Whereat he inly raged and as they talked
, False,,Smote him into the midriff with a stone
, False,,That beat out life he fell and deadly pale
, False,,Groaned out his soul with gushing blood effused
, False,,Much at that sight was Adam in his heart
, False,,Dismayed and thus in haste to the angel cried
, False,,Oh teacher some great mischief hath befallen
, False,,To that meek man who well had sacrificed
, False,,Is piety thus and pure devotion paid
, False,,To whom Michael thus he also moved replied
, False,,These two are brethren Adam and to come
, False,,Out of thy loins the unjust the just hath slain
, False,,For envy that his brothers offering found
, False,,From Heaven acceptance but the bloody fact
, False,,Will be avenged and the others faith approved
, False,,Lose no reward though here thou see him die
, False,,Rolling in dust and gore To which our sire
, False,,Alas both for the deed and for the cause
, False,,But have I now seen Death Is this the way
, False,,I must return to native dust Oh sight
, False,,Of terror foul and ugly to behold
, False,,Horrid to think how horrible to feel
, False,,To whom thus Michael Death thou hast seen
, False,,In his first shape on Man but many shapes
, False,,Of Death and many are the ways that lead
, False,,To his grim cave all dismal yet to sense
, False,,More terrible at the entrance than within
, False,,Some as thou sawest by violent stroke shall die
, False,,By fire flood famine by intemperance more
, False,,In meats and drinks which on the earth shall bring
, False,,Diseases dire of which a monstrous crew
, False,,Before thee shall appear that thou mayest know
, False,,What misery the inabstinence of Eve
, False,,Shall bring on Men Immediately a place
, False,,Before his eyes appeared sad noisome dark
, False,,A lazarhouse it seemed wherein were laid
, False,,Numbers of all diseased all maladies
, False,,Of ghastly spasm or racking torture qualms
, False,,Of heartsick agony all feverous kinds
, False,,Convulsions epilepsies fierce catarrhs
, False,,Intestine stone and ulcer colicpangs
, False,,Demoniac frenzy moping melancholy
, False,,And moonstruck madness pining atrophy
, False,,Marasmus and widewasting pestilence
, False,,Dropsies and asthmas and jointracking rheums
, False,,Dire was the tossing deep the groans Despair
, False,,Tended the sick busiest from couch to couch
, False,,And over them triumphant Death his dart
, False,,Shook but delayed to strike though oft invoked
, False,,With vows as their chief good and final hope
, False,,Sight so deform what heart of rock could long
, False,,Dryeyed behold Adam could not but wept
, False,,Though not of woman born compassion quelled
, False,,His best of man and gave him up to tears
, False,,A space till firmer thoughts restrained excess
, False,,And scarce recovering words his plaint renewed
, False,,Oh miserable mankind to what fall
, False,,Degraded to what wretched state reserved
, False,,Better end here unborn Why is life given
, False,,To be thus wrested from us rather why
, False,,Obtruded on us thus who if we knew
, False,,What we receive would either no accept
, False,,Life offered or soon beg to lay it down
, False,,Glad to be so dismissed in peace Can thus
, False,,The image of God in Man created once
, False,,So goodly and erect though faulty since
, False,,To such unsightly sufferings be debased
, False,,Under inhuman pains Why should not Man
, False,,Retaining still divine similitude
, False,,In part from such deformities be free
, False,,And for his Makers image sake exempt
, False,,Their Makers image answered Michael then
, False,,Forsook them when themselves they vilified
, False,,To serve ungoverned Appetite and took
, False,,His image whom they served a brutish vice
, False,,Inductive mainly to the sin of Eve
, False,,Therefore so abject is their punishment
, False,,Disfiguring not Gods likeness but their own
, False,,Or if his likeness by themselves defaced
, False,,While they pervert pure Natures healthful rules
, False,,To loathsome sickness worthily since they
, False,,Gods image did not reverence in themselves
, False,,I yield it just said Adam and submit
, False,,But is there yet no other way besides
, False,,These painful passages how we may come
, False,,To death and mix with our connatural dust
, False,,There is said Michael if thou well observe
, False,,The rule of Not too much by temperance taught
, False,,In what thou eatest and drinkest seeking from thence
, False,,Due nourishment not gluttonous delight
, False,,Till many years over thy head return
, False,,So mayest thou live till like ripe fruit thou drop
, False,,Into thy mothers lap or be with ease
, False,,Gathered nor harshly plucked for death mature
, False,,This is Old Age but then thou must outlive
, False,,Thy youth thy strength thy beauty which will change
, False,,To withered weak and gray thy senses then
, False,,Obtuse all taste of pleasure must forego
, False,,To what thou hast and for the air of youth
, False,,Hopeful and cheerful in thy blood will reign
, False,,A melancholy damp of cold and dry
, False,,To weigh thy spirits down and last consume
, False,,The balm of life To whom our ancestor
, False,,Henceforth I fly not death nor would prolong
, False,,Life much bent rather how I may be quit
, False,,Fairest and easiest of this cumbrous charge
, False,,Which I must keep till my appointed day
, False,,Of rendering up and patiently attend
, False,,My dissolution Michael replied
, False,,Nor love thy life nor hate but what thou livest
, False,,Live well how long or short permit to Heaven
, False,,And now prepare thee for another sight
, False,,He looked and saw a spacious plain whereon
, False,,Were tents of various hue by some were herds
, False,,Of cattle grazing others whence the sound
, False,,Of instruments that made melodious chime
, False,,Was heard of harp and organ and who moved
, False,,Their stops and chords was seen his volant touch
, False,,Instinct through all proportions low and high
, False,,Fled and pursued transverse the resonant fugue
, False,,In other part stood one who at the forge
, False,,Laboring two massy clods of iron and brass
, False,,Had melted whether found where casual fire
, False,,Had wasted woods on mountain or in vale
, False,,Down to the veins of earth thence gliding hot
, False,,To some caves mouth or whether washed by stream
, False,,From underground the liquid ore he drained
, False,,Into fit moulds prepared from which he formed
, False,,First his own tools then what might else be wrought
, False,,Fusil or graven in metal After these
, False,,But on the hither side a different sort
, False,,From the high neighboring hills which was their seat
, False,,Down to the plain descended by their guise
, False,,Just men they seemed and all their study bent
, False,,To worship God aright and know his works
, False,,Not hid nor those things last which might preserve
, False,,Freedom and peace to Men they on the plain
, False,,Long had not walked when from the tents behold
, False,,A bevy of fair women richly gay
, False,,In gems and wanton dress to the harp they sung
, False,,Soft amorous ditties and in dance came on
, False,,The men though grave eyed them and let their eyes
, False,,Rove without rein till in the amorous net
, False,,Fast caught they liked and each his liking chose
, False,,And now of love they treat till the eveningstar
, False,,Loves harbinger appeared then all in heat
, False,,They light the nuptial torch and bid invoke
, False,,Hymen then first to marriage rites invoked
, False,,With feast and music all the tents resound
, False,,Such happy interview and fair event
, False,,Of love and youth not lost songs garlands flowers
, False,,And charming symphonies attached the heart
, False,,Of Adam soon inclined to admit delight
, False,,The bent of nature which he thus expressed
, False,,True opener of mine eyes prime angel blest
, False,,Much better seems this vision and more hope
, False,,Of peaceful days portends than those two past
, False,,Those were of hate and death or pain much worse
, False,,Here Nature seems fulfilled in all her ends
, False,,To whom thus Michael Judge not what is best
, False,,By pleasure though to nature seeming meet
, False,,Created as thou art to nobler end
, False,,Holy and pure conformity divine
, False,,Those tents thou sawest so pleasant were the tents
, False,,Of wickedness wherein shall dwell his race
, False,,Who slew his brother studious they appear
, False,,Of arts that polish life inventers rare
, False,,Unmindful of their Maker though his Spirit
, False,,Taught them but they his gifts acknowledged none
, False,,Yet they a beauteous offspring shall beget
, False,,For that fair female troop thou sawest that seemed
, False,,Of Goddesses so blithe so smooth so gay
, False,,Yet empty of all good wherein consists
, False,,Womans domestic honor and chief praise
, False,,Bred only and completed to the taste
, False,,Of lustful appetence to sing to dance
, False,,To dress and troll the tongue and roll the eye
, False,,To these that sober race of men whose lives
, False,,Religious titled them the sons of God
, False,,Shall yield up all their virtue all their fame
, False,,Ignobly to the trains and to the smiles
, False,,Of these fair atheists and now swim in joy
, False,,Erelong to swim at large and laugh for which
, False,,The world erelong a world of tears must weep
, False,,To whom thus Adam of short joy bereft
, False,,Oh pity and shame that they who to live well
, False,,Entered so fair should turn aside to tread
, False,,Paths indirect or in the mid way faint
, False,,But still I see the tenor of Mans woe
, False,,Holds on the same from Woman to begin
, False,,From Mans effeminate slackness it begins
, False,,Said the angel who should better hold his place
, False,,By wisdom and superior gifts received
, False,,But now prepare thee for another scene
, False,,He looked and saw wide territory spread
, False,,Before him towns and rural works between
, False,,Cities of men with lofty gates and towers
, False,,Concourse in arms fierce faces threatening war
, False,,Giants of mighty bone and bold emprise
, False,,Part wield their arms part curb the foaming steed
, False,,Single or in array of battle ranged
, False,,Both horse and foot nor idly mustering stood
, False,,One way a band select from forage drives
, False,,A herd of beeves fair oxen and fair kine
, False,,From a fat meadow ground or fleecy flock
, False,,Ewes and their bleating lambs over the plain
, False,,Their booty scarce with life the shepherds fly
, False,,But call in aid which makes a bloody fray
, False,,With cruel tournament the squadrons join
, False,,Where cattle pastured late now scattered lies
, False,,With carcasses and arms the ensanguined field
, False,,Deserted Others to a city strong
, False,,Lay siege encamped by battery scale and mine
, False,,Assaulting others from the wall defend
, False,,With dart and javelin stones and sulfurous fire
, False,,On each hand slaughter and gigantic deeds
, False,,In other part the sceptered heralds call
, False,,To council in the citygates anon
, False,,Grayheaded men and grave with warriors mixed
, False,,Assemble and harangues are heard but soon
, False,,In factious opposition till at last
, False,,Of middle age one rising eminent
, False,,In wise deport spake much of right and wrong
, False,,Of justice or religion truth and peace
, False,,And judgment from above him old and young
, False,,Exploded and had seized with violent hands
, False,,Had not a cloud descending snatched him thence
, False,,Unseen amid the throng so violence
, False,,Proceeded and oppression and swordlaw
, False,,Through all the plain and refuge none was found
, False,,Adam was all in tears and to his guide
, False,,Lamenting turned full sad Oh what are these
, False,,Deaths ministers not men who thus deal death
, False,,Inhumanly to men and multiply
, False,,Ten thousandfold the sin of him who slew
, False,,His brother for of whom such massacre
, False,,Make they but of their brethren men of men
, False,,But who was that just man whom had not Heaven
, False,,Rescued had in his righteousness been lost
, False,,To whom thus Michael These are the product
, False,,Of those illmated marriages thou sawest
, False,,Where good with bad were matched who of themselves
, False,,Abhor to join and by imprudence mixed
, False,,Produce prodigious births of body or mind
, False,,Such were these giants men of high renown
, False,,For in those days might only shall be admired
, False,,And velour and heroic virtue called
, False,,To overcome in battle and subdue
, False,,Nations and bring home spoils with infinite
, False,,Manslaughter shall be held the highest pitch
, False,,Of human glory and for glory done
, False,,Of triumph to be styled great conquerors
, False,,Patrons of mankind Gods and sons of Gods
, False,,Destroyers rightlier called and plagues of men

, False,,With Earths wide bounds his glory with the Heavens
, False,,He ceased discerning Adam with such joy
, False,,Surcharged as had like grief been dewed in tears
, False,,Without the vent of words which these he breathed
, False,,Oh prophet of glad tidings finisher
, False,,Of utmost hope now clear I understand
, False,,What oft my steadiest thoughts have searched in vain
, False,,Why our great Expectation should be called
, False,,The seed of Woman Virgin Mother hail
, False,,High in the love of Heaven yet from my loins
, False,,Thou shalt proceed and from thy womb the Son
, False,,Of God Most High so God with man unites
, False,,Needs must the Serpent now his capital bruise
, False,,Expect with mortal pain Say where and when
, False,,Their fight what stroke shall bruise the victors heel
, False,,To whom thus Michael Dream not of their fight
, False,,As of a duel or the local wounds
, False,,Of head or heel Not therefore joins the Son
, False,,Manhood to Godhead with more strength to foil
, False,,Thy enemy nor so is overcome
, False,,Satan whose fall from Heaven a deadlier bruise
, False,,Disabled not to give thee thy deaths wound
, False,,Which he who comes thy Savior shall recur
, False,,Not by destroying Satan but his works
, False,,In thee and in thy seed Nor can this be
, False,,But by fulfilling that which thou didst want
, False,,Obedience to the law of God imposed
, False,,On penalty of death and suffering death
, False,,The penalty to thy transgression due
, False,,And due to theirs which out of thine will grow
, False,,So only can high Justice rest appaid
, False,,The law of God exact he shall fulfill
, False,,Both by obedience and by love though love
, False,,Alone fulfill the law thy punishment
, False,,He shall endure by coming in the flesh
, False,,To a reproachful life and cursed death
, False,,Proclaiming life to all who shall believe
, False,,In his redemption and that his obedience
, False,,Imputed becomes theirs by faith his merits
, False,,To save them not their own though legal works
, False,,For this he shall live hated be blasphemed
, False,,Seized on by force judged and to death condemned
, False,,A shameful and accursed nailed to the cross
, False,,By his own nation slain for bringing life
, False,,But to the cross he nails thy enemies
, False,,The law that is against thee and the sins
, False,,Of all mankind with him there crucified
, False,,Never to hurt them more who rightly trust
, False,,In this his satisfaction so he dies
, False,,But soon revives Death over him no power
, False,,Shall long usurp ere the third dawning light
, False,,Return the stars of morn shall see him rise
, False,,Out of his grave fresh as the dawning light
, False,,Thy ransom paid which man from death redeems
, False,,His death for Man as many as offered life
, False,,Neglect not and the benefit embrace
, False,,By faith not void of works This Godlike act
, False,,Annuls thy doom the death thou shouldest have died
, False,,In sin for ever lost from life this act
, False,,Shall bruise the head of Satan crush his strength
, False,,Defeating Sin and Death his two main arms
, False,,And fix far deeper in his head their stings
, False,,Than temporal death shall bruise the victors heel
, False,,Or theirs whom he redeems a death like sleep
, False,,A gentle wafting to immortal life
, False,,Nor after resurrection shall he stay
, False,,Longer on earth than certain times to appear
, False,,To his disciples men who in his life
, False,,Still followed him to them shall leave in charge
, False,,To teach all nations what of him they learned
, False,,And his salvation them who shall believe
, False,,Baptizing in the profluent stream the sign
, False,,Of washing them from guilt of sin to life
, False,,Pure and in mind prepared if so befall
, False,,For death like that which the Redeemer died
, False,,All nations they shall teach for from that day
, False,,Not only to the sons of Abrahams loins
, False,,Salvation shall be preached but to the sons
, False,,Of Abrahams faith wherever through the world
, False,,So in his seed all nations shall be blest
, False,,Then to the Heaven of Heavens he shall ascend
, False,,With victory triumphing through the air
, False,,Over his foes and thine there shall surprise
, False,,The Serpent prince of air and drag in chains
, False,,Through all his realm and there confounded leave
, False,,Then enter into glory and resume
, False,,His seat at Gods right hand exalted high
, False,,Above all names in Heaven and thence shall come
, False,,When this worlds dissolution shall be ripe
, False,,With glory and power to judge both quick and dead
, False,,To judge the unfaithful dead but to reward
, False,,His faithful and receive them into bliss
, False,,Whether in Heaven or Earth for then the Earth
, False,,Shall all be Paradise far happier place
, False,,Than this of Eden and far happier days
, False,,So spake the archangel Michael then paused
, False,,As at the worlds great period and our sire
, False,,Replete with joy and wonder thus replied
, False,,Oh goodness infinite goodness immense
, False,,That all this good of evil shall produce
, False,,And evil turn to good more wonderful
, False,,Than that which by creation first brought forth
, False,,Light out of darkness Full of doubt I stand
, False,,Whether I should repent me now of sin
, False,,By me done and occasioned or rejoice
, False,,Much more that much more good thereof shall spring
, False,,To God more glory more goodwill to men
, False,,From God and over wrath grace shall abound
, False,,But say if our Deliverer up to Heaven
, False,,Must reascend what will betide the few
, False,,His faithful left among the unfaithful herd
, False,,The enemies of truth Who then shall guide
, False,,His people who defend Will they not deal
, False,,Worse with his followers than with him they dealt
, False,,Be sure they will said the angel but from Heaven
, False,,He to his own a comforter will send
, False,,The promise of the Father who shall dwell
, False,,His Spirit within them and the law of faith
, False,,Working through love upon their hearts shall write
, False,,To guide them in all truth and also arm
, False,,With spiritual armor able to resist
, False,,Satans assaults and quench his fiery darts
, False,,What man can do against them not afraid
, False,,Though to the death against such cruelties
, False,,With inward consolations recompensed
, False,,And oft supported so as shall amaze
, False,,Their proudest persecutors For the Spirit
, False,,Poured first on his Apostles whom he sends
, False,,To evangelize the nations then on all
, False,,Baptized shall them with wondrous gifts endue
, False,,To speak all tongues and do all miracles
, False,,As did their Lord before them Thus they win
, False,,Great numbers of each nation to receive
, False,,With joy the tidings brought from Heaven At length
, False,,Their ministry performed and race well run
, False,,Their doctrine and their story written left
, False,,They die but in their room as they forewarn
, False,,Wolves shall succeed for teachers grievous wolves
, False,,Who all the sacred mysteries of Heaven
, False,,To their own vile advantages shall turn
, False,,Of lucre and ambition and the truth
, False,,With superstitions and traditions taint
, False,,Left only in those written records pure
, False,,Though not but by the Spirit understood
, False,,Then shall they seek to avail themselves of names
, False,,Places and titles and with these to join
, False,,Secular power though feigning still to act
, False,,By spiritual to themselves appropriating
, False,,The Spirit of God promised alike and given
, False,,To all believers and from that pretence
, False,,Spiritual laws by carnal power shall force
, False,,On every conscience laws which none shall find
, False,,Left them inrolled or what the Spirit within
, False,,Shall on the heart engrave What will they then
, False,,But force the Spirit of Grace itself and bind
, False,,His consort Liberty what but unbuild
, False,,His living temples built by faith to stand
, False,,Their own faith not anothers for on earth
, False,,Who against faith and conscience can be heard
, False,,Infallible yet many will presume
, False,,Whence heavy persecution shall arise
, False,,On all who in the worship persevere
, False,,Of spirit and truth the rest far greater part
, False,,Will deem in outward rites and specious forms
, False,,Religion satisfied Truth shall retire
, False,,Bestuck with slanderous darts and works of faith
, False,,Rarely be found So shall the world go on
, False,,To good malignant to bad men benign
, False,,Under her own weight groaning till the day
, False,,Appear of respiration to the just
, False,,And vengeance to the wicked at return
, False,,Of him so lately promised to thy aid
, False,,The Womans Seed obscurely then foretold
, False,,Now ampler known thy Savior and thy Lord
, False,,Last in the clouds from Heaven to be revealed
, False,,In glory of the Father to dissolve
, False,,Satan with his perverted world then raise
, False,,From the conflagrant mass purged and refined
, False,,New Heavens new Earth ages of endless date
, False,,Founded in righteousness and peace and love
, False,,To bring forth fruits joy and eternal bliss
, False,,He ended and thus Adam last replied
, False,,How soon hath thy prediction Seer blest
, False,,Measured this transient world the race of time
, False,,Till time stand fixed Beyond is all abyss
, False,,Eternity whose end no eye can reach
, False,,Greatlyinstructed I shall hence depart
, False,,Greatly in peace of thought and have my fill
, False,,Of knowledge what this vessel can contain
, False,,Beyond which was my folly to aspire
, False,,Henceforth I learn that to obey is best
, False,,And love with fear the only God to walk
, False,,As in his presence ever to observe
, False,,His providence and on him sole depend
, False,,Merciful over all his works with good
, False,,Still overcoming evil and by small
, False,,Accomplishing great things by things deemed weak
, False,,Subverting worldly strong and worldly wise
, False,,By simply meek that suffering for truths sake
, False,,Is fortitude to highest victory
, False,,And to the faithful death the gate of life
, False,,Taught this by his example whom I now
, False,,Acknowledge my Redeemer ever blest
, False,,To whom thus also the angel last replied
, False,,This having learned thou hast attained the sum
, False,,Of wisdom hope no higher though all the stars
, False,,Thou knewest by name and all the ethereal powers
, False,,All secrets of the deep all Natures works
, False,,Or works of God in Heaven air earth or sea
, False,,And all the riches of this world enjoyedst
, False,,And all the rule one empire only add
, False,,Deeds to thy knowledge answerable add faith
, False,,Add virtue patience temperance add love
, False,,By name to come called charity the soul
, False,,Of all the rest then wilt thou not be loath
, False,,To leave this Paradise but shalt possess
, False,,A Paradise within thee happier far
, False,,Let us descend now therefore from this top
, False,,Of speculation for the hour precise
, False,,Exacts our parting hence and see the guards
, False,,By me encamped on yonder hill expect
, False,,Their motion at whose front a flaming sword
, False,,In signal of remove waves fiercely round
, False,,We may no longer stay go waken Eve
, False,,Her also I with gentle dreams have calmed
, False,,Portending good and all her spirits composed
, False,,To meek submission thou at season fit
, False,,Let her with thee partake what thou hast heard
, False,,Chiefly what may concern her faith to know
, False,,The great deliverance by her seed to come
, False,,For by the Womans seed on all mankind
, False,,That ye may live which will be many days
, False,,Both in one faith unanimous though sad
, False,,With cause for evils past yet much more cheered
, False,,With meditation on the happy end
, False,,He ended and they both descend the hill
, False,,Descended Adam to the bower where Eve
, False,,Lay sleeping ran before but found her waked
, False,,And thus with words not sad she him received
, False,,Whence thou returnest and whither wentest I know
, False,,For God is also in sleep and dreams advise
, False,,Which he hath sent propitious some great good
, False,,Presaging since with sorrow and hearts distress
, False,,Wearied I fell asleep But now lead on
, False,,In me is no delay with thee to go
, False,,Is to stay here without thee here to stay
, False,,Is to go hence unwilling thou to me
, False,,Art all things under Heaven all places thou
, False,,Who for my willful crime art banished hence
, False,,This further consolation yet secure
, False,,I carry hence though all by me is lost
, False,,Such favor I unworthy am vouchsafed
, False,,By me the Promised Seed shall all restore
, False,,So spake our mother Eve and Adam heard
, False,,Well pleased but answered not For now too nigh
, False,,The archangel stood and from the other hill
, False,,To their fixed station all in bright array
, False,,The Cherubim descended on the ground
, False,,Gliding meteorous as eveningmist
, False,,Risen from a river oer the marsh glides
, False,,And gathers ground fast at the laborer’s heel
, False,,Homeward returning High in front advanced
, False,,The brandished sword of God before them blazed
, False,,Fierce as a comet which with torrid heat
, False,,And vapor as the Libyan air adust
, False,,Began to parch that temperate clime whereat
, False,,In either hand the hastening angel caught
, False,,Our lingering parents and to the eastern gate
, False,,Led them direct and down the cliff as fast
, False,,To the subjected plain then disappeared
, False,,They looking back all the eastern side beheld
, False,,Of Paradise so late their happy seat
, False,,Waved over by that flaming brand the gate
, False,,With dreadful faces thronged and fiery arms
, False,,Some natural tears they dropt but wiped them soon
, False,,The world was all before them where to choose
, False,,Their place of rest and Providence their guide
, False,,They hand in hand with wandering
